Jixian Local Militia Attacks Poor People's Association Base

(Peiping) After the Jixian Poor People's Association was banned by the authorities, a group of about 100 people suddenly appeared in the afternoon of the day before yesterday, carrying firearms, and surrounded the Public Security Bureau in the Fourth District of Jixian County, intending to disarm it. The Sixth District Militia and the He An Team arrived and dispersed them, arresting more than 60 people and sending them to the county government for detention. The militia and security team are advancing towards the Poor People's Association base in Dayuzhuang, preparing for a thorough resolution. (24th Dispatch)

(Peiping) More than 100 armed rioters from the Jixian Poor People's Association surrounded the district office and public security station in the Fourth District of the county on the evening of the 22nd. The Sixth District Militia and the police team cooperated to suppress them, and a conflict occurred immediately. After a long standoff, one person was killed and one injured on the militia side, and there were also casualties among the Poor People's Association rioters. More than 60 people were arrested on the spot and taken to the county seat, where they were detained in the county government's special detention center. They are currently being interrogated. The security team has advanced towards the headquarters of the Poor People's Association in Dayuzhuang. It is reported that the rioters of the association are scattered due to the strict search by the authorities. There are still hundreds of remnants with complete firearms, many of whom are reactionary elements. It is heard that Communist Xuan Xiafu is secretly manipulating them in Luandong. (24th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Old Capital Cultural Relics Reorganization Committee to be Established

Starting with the Reorganization of Altars and Temples and City Towers

(Peiping) The Old Capital Cultural Relics Reorganization Committee will soon be established. The candidates for the committee members will be Huang Fu, Yuan Liang, Yu Xuezhong, Song Zheyuan, and representatives from the five ministries of Interior, Communications, Finance, Railways, and Education as ex officio members. Huang will be the chairman, and several full-time members will be hired. The steps for reorganizing the cultural relics in the old capital are planned to start with the repair of the altars and temples and the city towers, and then build the main trunk roads from Peiping to the Western Hills, to Tangshan, to Nanyuan, and to the main thoroughfares in the urban area. For the convenience of international tourists visiting Peiping, a large-scale tour company and museum are also planned to be established. Yingtai in Zhongnanhai will be used as the museum site, and a theater will be built elsewhere, with the aim of preserving and promoting China's inherent theatrical culture. The establishment of the tour company is currently being negotiated for investment by Shanghai Bank and Jincheng Bank. The museum is planned to be located in the Taimiao (Imperial Ancestral Temple). Inside, maps of Peiping and models of various buildings will be displayed as a reference for tourists visiting Peiping. A cultural commodity market will also be set up to control the sale of cultural commodities. The construction cost of the museum is estimated at 300,000 yuan. The municipal government has scheduled a cultural commodity exhibition in April next year. The reorganization of cultural relics in the old capital is planned to be 3.09 million yuan, with 1 million yuan allocated by the Ministry of Finance, 1.09 million yuan by the Ministry of Railways, and the remainder by the Peiping Municipality. It will be completed in two phases, each lasting six months. The first phase of the project is scheduled to be completed from September to April next year, and the second phase from April to September of the following year, to realize the entire Peiping tourist area plan. The address of the Cultural Relics Reorganization Committee will be located within the Political Reorganization Committee. (24th Dispatch)

Central and National Government Memorial Weeks Reports

Chairman Lin Elaborates on Inherent Morality

Ding Chao-wu Reports on the Situation in Jiangxi Province

(Nanjing) The National Government held a memorial week on the morning of the 24th, attended by He Yingqin, Chen Xunyong, Lin Xiang, Lu Chao, Wei Huai, and other officials from various Yuan, Ministries, and Commissions, totaling more than 500 people. Chairman Lin led the ceremony and then gave a detailed elaboration on the relationship between Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings on national rejuvenation and morality. First, he said that morality is inherent in our country and there is no such thing as new or old. In general, it consists of the four characters of courtesy, righteousness, integrity, and shame. The ancients regarded them as the four dimensions of a country. If a country cannot earnestly practice these four characters, there is no one that will not decline. The eight characters of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, peace, and harmony are extended from the four characters of courtesy, righteousness, integrity, and shame in order to realize world peace. Second, he said that people today have many misunderstandings about the so-called new morality of freedom, equality, etc. Freedom has limits and cannot be exceeded. Equality also has a scope and should be observed. Finally, he said that the Chinese people must deeply understand and practice their inherent morality, and then the nation can have hope of rejuvenation. He also encouraged his colleagues to follow Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, deeply reflect, and not exceed the moral standards in every move. (24th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central Government held its 162nd memorial week at 9:00 AM on the morning of the 24th, attended by Central Committee members Ye Chucang, Fang Juehui, Zhang Ji, Hong Ludong, Li Zonghuang, Wang Qi, Li Ciwen, Ding Chao-wu, and all staff members, totaling approximately 500 people. Chairman Ye Chucang and Ding Chao-wu reported on the recent political and military situation in Jiangxi Province, stating briefly that Jiangxi Province has made significant progress in all aspects recently. According to my observation, there are approximately the following points: (1) The reason why the military bandit suppression has progressed so rapidly this time and can eliminate bandit troubles is that the bandit suppression officers and soldiers can cooperate with the people. This is the effective result of the training provided by the military officer corps founded by Chairman Chiang. (2) In terms of politics, it can organize the people and use the people, such as building roads and handling Baojia, etc., to achieve results. (3) In terms of party affairs, it has recently trained workers to run children's remedial education and promoted various new life movement activities, also with success. This progress in Jiangxi Province is because the entire province, from top to bottom, can embrace the three spirits of creativity, construction, and seeking rapid results, and strive to engage in it. It is hoped that the people of the country, whether for the party or the country, should embrace this spirit, and then the nation can be rejuvenated. After the speech, the meeting adjourned at 10:00 AM. (24th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance to Advance Military and Political Expenses for This Month

Customs in Various Places Investigate and Seize With Unusual Strictness

No Large-Scale Smuggling Has Been Discovered Recently

(Nanjing) According to the Customs Service, since the prohibition of tax evasion, customs investigations and seizures in various places have been unusually strict. In the past four or five months, smuggling may still be unavoidable, but it is small. Large-scale tax evasion has not been discovered. The reason why the tax revenue has not improved since the change in tax rates this year is actually due to the weak domestic purchasing power and the reduction of imports. The general situation of the tax revenue in the months of July, August, September is actually the same as in the 23rd year. After October, the Tax Service has not yet reported. However, in the past, after October has always been a slow month. The tax revenue after setting up checkpoints along the Great Wall in North China is not very much. However, the purpose of setting up the various checkpoints was originally to prevent smuggling and tax evasion. Since the prohibition of silver exports and the implementation of anti-smuggling, it has been effective. The Tax Service has sent personnel to various customs offices to inspect. Large-scale smuggling has disappeared. If legitimate merchants export silver, they must have a permit from the Ministry. The effect has also been achieved since the recent limit on private carrying. The general public's so-called lack of cash, suspected of being caused by the unabated smuggling, is just speculation. It is indeed true that there is a greater need for cash in the silver market after the autumn harvest and agricultural products are sold into the market. This has always been the custom and cannot be immediately regarded as the impact of too many exports. (24th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Customs has recently been severely affected by the proliferation of smuggled goods, which has greatly impacted the national treasury. It has specially formulated a reward for informants method, notifying merchants and residents to know. If it is seized after being reported, 40% of the auctioned price of the goods will be used as a bonus. It has also instructed the outer class personnel to step up anti-smuggling in order to prevent the import of smuggled goods. (24th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Nanjing Court to Transfer Key Suspects in Yi Case

Russia-Manchukuo Conference on Waterway Issues Concludes

Delta Issue Unresolved

(Harbin) The Russia-Manchukuo conference on waterway issues has been held in Daheihe since October 9th for a total of 14 times. An agreement on the waterway has now been reached. Because the area is a military stronghold, the Russian side ignored it. This matter could not be resolved. It is heard that Horiuchi, the Japanese chairman of the Manchukuo delegation to the waterway conference, is scheduled to depart for Harbin on the 27th. (24th China United Press Dispatch)

Soviet Russia Detains Japanese Officers on the Banks of the Ussuri River

Suspected of Espionage for Secretly Photographing Terrain

Sent to Border Defense Headquarters for Interrogation

(Moscow) A new incident has occurred on the Russo-Manchurian border, further complicating the Japanese-Russian dispute. An investigation is currently underway. According to a telegram from Khabarovsk to the government, Soviet Russian officials are investigating the actions of a Japanese military officer and a "Manchukuo" soldier who were suddenly discovered in a small border village called Volkovo-Nikolskoye. It is alleged that the Japanese officer was taking photographs in the village while the "Manchukuo" soldier was recording notes nearby. Both men have been detained by local Soviet Russian authorities. Soviet Russian officials claim that the officer was carrying a military saber and a pistol, as well as a camera and several unused film rolls. Additionally, a photographic map of the vicinity was found, detailing the geographical features of the Russo-Manchurian border, along with a notebook written in Japanese. According to the two men, they crossed the border in search of a five-year-old child and two farmers who had also crossed the border and were detained by Soviet Russian authorities. The two men are currently being held locally pending orders from Moscow. (National Telegram, 24th)

Khabarovsk, December 21st. A Japanese military officer and his attendant were detained by Soviet forces on the banks of the Ussuri River in the village of Verkhni Spasskoye, 30 kilometers south of Iman. They entered the home of a collective farmer, Kovalev, seeking a drink, and then proceeded to the center of the village. The officer began taking photographs while his attendant recorded notes on paper. Upon detention, the officer was found to be carrying a bayonet and a pistol, a camera and five rolls of film, and a military satchel containing a topographical map of the Sino-Soviet border annotated in Japanese, as well as a Japanese notebook. The attendant was also carrying a bayonet. According to the Japanese officer, he crossed the border in search of a seven-year-old child who had escaped from a Chinese thatched house (opposite Verkhne-Nikolskoye village) a few days prior. He was also searching for a Korean and a Chinese person who had been detained by Soviet border guards a week earlier. The Japanese officer has been transported by automobile to the Border Defense Headquarters for further interrogation. (TASS Telegram, 23rd)

General Minami Jiro Explains Policy Toward Manchuria

Visits Ugaki in Korea En Route

Seoul: Before arriving in Seoul on the 23rd, the Commander of the Kwantung Army, Minami Jiro, expressed his aspirations in the car, stating that his ambition upon assuming his post is to achieve complete emotional and economic integration between Japan and Manchuria. He is determined to dedicate his efforts to this goal. The reason for passing through Korea is twofold: Firstly, Manchuria and Korea share a border, and cooperation is impossible without mutual understanding. Therefore, he must meet with Governor-General Ugaki for earnest discussions. Secondly, as the end of the year approaches, he is eager to assume his post. "Manchukuo" is an independent nation inseparable from Japan. This goes without saying. It is Japan's national policy to maintain close contact with this friendly nation in terms of politics, economy, security, and transportation, and to provide guidance. It is the duty of those on the ground to fully consult with "Manchukuo" on this matter. Close contact, in other words, means that without complete and comprehensive interaction between the Japanese and Manchurian peoples, problems such as the influx of Korean farmers into Manchuria may arise. He has been thoroughly studying this issue and intends to openly exchange views with Governor-General Ugaki. The Governor-General is a dedicated researcher, and he may have considerable insights. In short, provided that both parties proceed from the perspective of desiring the sound development of "Manchukuo," there is no doubt that mutual understanding will be established. Furthermore, he questions whether it is appropriate to rely solely on swords and guns to protect the border with this inseparable independent nation. While security may be necessary, such a confrontational atmosphere is unpleasant. He intends to convey his views to the Governor-General on this matter. The Chientao region is policed by Korean troops because Koreans account for half of the population there. Therefore, the demarcation of the area between Japan and Manchuria has been proposed. When he was the Commander of the Korean Army, he firmly believed that the solution to the Asian continental problem lay in the Chientao issue. However, after the Manchurian Incident, administrative changes have occurred. At present, the continental problem can only be resolved with the sound and long-term development of "Manchukuo." Extraterritoriality inevitably poses an obstacle to the harmony between the Japanese and Manchurian peoples, and it is necessary to remove this obstacle. (Dentsu Telegram, 23rd)

The 67th Session of the Japanese Diet Convenes

Hamada of the Seiyukai Party Elected Speaker of the House

(Tokyo) The 67th session of the Diet convened today. This is the first ordinary session of the Diet under the Okada Cabinet. The Seiyukai's explosive motion in the previous extraordinary session clearly demonstrated its attitude towards the government. It is uncertain what actions they will take this time as an opposition party, and the government cannot be optimistic. The election of the speaker today has attracted much attention. However, the year may pass peacefully. The atmosphere will certainly become tense when the Diet reconvenes early next year, as the Seiyukai plans to pressure the government to submit supplementary budget requests. In that case, the government may have to dissolve the Diet. According to government sources, if the government advocates dissolution, the Seiyukai's attitude will soften. Despite some twists and turns, the Diet can achieve a satisfactory outcome. (Domei Telegram, 24th)

(Tokyo) The ordinary session of the Diet convened at 9:00 AM today. After the House of Peers determined the selection of chairmen and directors for each faction, it notified the government and the House of Representatives. The House of Representatives convened at 10:00 AM. Due to the resignation of Speaker Akita, the speaker was elected today. The Seiyukai nominated Hamada Kunimatsu as its candidate. The Minseito Party refused the Seiyukai's request for cooperation and nominated its own member as a candidate. As a result, Hamada was elected with an absolute majority. (Domei Telegram, 24th)

(Tokyo) Hamada Kunimatsu, who was elected Speaker of the House of Representatives today, made the following statement:

Regarding the proper utilization of the system of continuing committees or newly established standing committees, this has been my long-standing belief. I intend to make every effort to obtain the consent of the House of Peers and strive to realize this. As for the administrative branch, in light of the current situation, if the National Policy Deliberation Council is deemed necessary, then such an agency must also be established within the legislature, the Diet. I believe this is the natural trend. (Domei Telegram, 24th)

Japan Revitalizes Diplomacy

Establishes Foreign Ministry Advisory Council

To Serve as Consultation for the Foreign Minister

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs previously established a System Efficiency Renovation Committee, with Vice Minister Shigemitsu as chairman and Treaty Bureau Director Kuriyama as vice-chairman, and the most senior section chiefs of each bureau as members. The committee is researching reforms to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' current system, as well as specific plans to improve efficiency. Once concrete plans are formulated, they will be implemented immediately. The system of roving ambassadors, which was previously decided upon, was also a product of this committee. This time, the Ministry will further establish, through internal regulations, a council of senior envoys currently in the country or awaiting assignment, to meet regularly once a month, listen to reports from executives on the progress of important diplomatic issues, exchange opinions, and answer inquiries from the Foreign Minister. The reason for establishing this council is to give it the function of a military council of senior officers from various military branches. In addition, the Kasumigaseki Association, an organization composed of current and former high-ranking officials, lacks organized function. Therefore, it is planned to reorganize its external organization, much like a veterans' association. Foreign Minister Hirota is shifting from the previous emphasis on improving overseas legations to prioritizing the improvement of domestic agencies to determine diplomatic policy. He intends to use the aforementioned advisory and auxiliary bodies, in addition to the Ministry, to thoroughly convey the Ministry's policy to the public while also reflecting the public's intentions in diplomacy. (Dentsu Telegram, 24th)

Japanese Red Scare

Mass Arrests of Communists in Aichi Prefecture

Fifty-Eight Indicted

(Tokyo) The news ban on the communist movement incident in Aichi Prefecture has been lifted today. The communist movement in the prefecture was organized around Mr. Tatsuo Iwata in June of last year, establishing the Nagoya District Council of the National Council. Party members were ordered to infiltrate various important factories to conduct activities. After discovering this, the police authorities began investigations at 9:00 PM on February 24th of this year, arresting 1725 people. As a result of the investigation, 58 of them were indicted under the Maintenance of Public Order Law. (Dentsu Telegram, 24th)

Japan and Russia Negotiate Details of Chinese Eastern Railway Sale

(Tokyo) Mr. Galashevsky, the Soviet representative in the Chinese Eastern Railway negotiations, visited Mr. Togo, the Director of the Asian Bureau of the Foreign Ministry, at 2:00 PM on the 24th. He held discussions regarding the details, based on instructions from his government, and then departed. (Domei Telegram, 24th)

Current Affairs Commentary

The Palace Museum Theft Case Must Be Strictly Punished

The Palace Museum theft scandal, which has caused an uproar both domestically and internationally, has already been fully investigated by the court and has been prosecuted. However, the defendants, Yi Peiji, Li Zongtong, and others, have consistently refused to appear in court. Their guilt is evident, and no amount of justification can acquit them. As high-ranking officials of the state, the fact that Yi and his accomplices engaged in embezzlement and theft already constitutes an inexcusable crime. Moreover, taking advantage of the emergency situation in North China and engaging in looting amidst the chaos makes their actions even more unforgivable.

The treasures of the Palace Museum represent the embodiment of the efforts of our ancestors. Some are helpful for scholarly research, while others are beneficial for historical verification. The essence of thousands of years of careful preservation, untouched by floods, fires, or war, has been reduced to nothing through the theft, sale, and embezzlement by a small number of individuals. The impact on the nation's culture and the harm to the national spirit are immense. Therefore, the crimes of Yi and his cohorts are many times more egregious than those who desecrate ancestral graves and steal treasures. The government has recently increased the penalties for grave robbers and bandits who hold firearms and act in groups of three or more, sentencing them to death. Those who make grave robbing a regular occupation are also sentenced to life imprisonment. However, Yi and his accomplices, sheltered by the concessions and foreign extraterritorial rights, are able to live comfortably and carefree. If this matter is not strictly investigated, how can national discipline be enforced and justice be served in this era?

Yi and his accomplices were initially pursued by the High Court, impeached by the Control Yuan, and subsequently prosecuted by the Jiangning District Court and thoroughly investigated by the Central Political Council, and most recently investigated by the Central Antiquities Preservation Association. If they were not guilty of embezzlement and theft, they could have come forward and defended themselves in court to prove their innocence. However, they have not done so, which indicates their guilt. Furthermore, even if they had acted out of temporary private desires and committed this inappropriate act, they could have confessed their crimes afterward, returned the stolen goods, and perhaps the people of the country would have been willing to offer them a chance to start anew amidst their unforgivable deeds. However, they have been blinded by greed and have never considered doing so. After the incident came to light, they only knew how to exploit the concessions and foreign extraterritorial rights, as well as the provision in criminal procedure law that prohibits judgments in absentia, refusing to respond to summonses in order to delay the pronouncement of their sentences. Recently, there have been reports that Yi himself has fled to the puppet state of Manchukuo, further revealing the insidious nature of his intentions.

We have also heard that a portion of the stolen antiquities had been shipped to France for secret sale. However, due to a lack of secrecy, the plan failed. The items were discovered by customs officials in Marseille and have been detained ever since. In late October, newspapers in both the North and South reported that Xiao Yu, the former director of the Beiping Agricultural Experiment Station, was the mastermind behind the operation. However, Xiao has recently issued notices in the newspapers vehemently denying the allegations and proclaiming his innocence. Xiao Yu was previously accused of colluding with Yi Peiji to embezzle public funds and was a co-defendant with Yi in a case prosecuted by the Jiangning District Court. Although there was no mention of him conspiring with Yi to steal treasures at that time, there is no doubt about the close relationship between him and Yi. As for the fact that antiquities were seized in France, the Central Antiquities Preservation Association has obtained many pieces of conclusive evidence. The truth will eventually come to light. However, we are unwilling to comment further until the truth is clarified. Regarding the theft case, Xiao Xiangpei and Liu Guang'e have been arrested and brought to justice. We hope that the central government will take swift and effective measures to arrest all the key perpetrators of the case, ensuring that none escape. Those who are hiding in the concessions or have fled abroad should be extradited and punished accordingly. Xiao Yu is a suspect and a co-defendant in the embezzlement case, and he should not be treated lightly either.

Countries Worldwide Celebrate Christmas

British King Hosts Feast for 700 Poor People in Palace

Germany also hosts 12,000 Poor Children

Austria Pardons Over 6,000 Political Prisoners

Train Collisions and Plane Crashes in United States

Bethlehem: The entire world will celebrate Christmas tonight via radio. This great church has meticulously arranged for the broadcasting of various ceremonies. In the center of the church is a replica of the Holy Grotto, said to be built on the site where Jesus was born. The service will begin at midnight. The small town has been visited by thousands of pilgrims from all over the world, including Abyssinian Christians, Anglo-Saxons, Armenians, Roman Catholics, and members of various denominations, all wearing different attire and speaking different languages. Many have come from Germany, including many expelled Jews. As for Italy, due to the convenience of the newly established direct air route to Palestine, many have also come. This year's celebration emphasizes prosperity. In the past, female pilgrims would trudge through the dust on foot, but now they travel by vehicles. This year, there are two newly built roads, and pilgrims mostly travel on new public buses or in their own cars. The newly built roads are lit with electric lights, extending from Jerusalem to Bethlehem. The locals are also dressed more lavishly than in previous years. In addition, one other thing reflects prosperity: the mayor of Bethlehem will also participate in the service. Bethlehem will also hold its first mayoral election this year. In the past few weeks, Christian churches throughout Palestine have spared no effort in decorating and arranging, with the wealthy Armenians being the most extravagant. Female pilgrims have been arriving from Jerusalem in a continuous stream, all hoping to enter the Holy Grotto, but the Holy Grotto is very small, only accommodating six people at a time. Therefore, most female pilgrims can only catch a glimpse of the Holy Grotto before returning. (National Telegram, 24th)

London: Christmas 1934, regardless of the weather, is certainly a happy holiday in England, as stores, railways, and transportation businesses across the country are reporting exceptionally brisk business. According to a report from the Bank of London, the amount of currency in circulation has now reached £402,000,000, which is the highest figure since 1921. In comparison, the amount of currency in circulation during Christmas 1932 was £370,000,000, and in 1933 it was £390,000,000. This year, the supply of goods is abundant and cheaper than last year. Major stores in London are displaying attractive goods, and business is excellent. The same is true in Manchester and other parts of the North. The thick fog of yesterday has dissipated today, but the weather is unusually mild for this time of year, with no snowy Christmas scenes of the past. Today, the British King is hosting a Christmas tea party at Buckingham Palace, inviting 700 poor people, as per tradition. The London Police Department's Detective Squad has a light workload due to the holiday, so only 25 of the 500 officers are on duty at the station. However, in case of an emergency, 300 officers can be summoned within ten minutes. The situation in Warsaw is not so peaceful. The Warsaw police today arrested 200 notorious thieves and imprisoned them for ten days. However, the police donated funds to purchase food and drink for them, allowing them to spend a happy New Year in prison. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

Vienna: To celebrate Christmas, the Austrian government today released over 6,000 Social Democrats and National Socialists held in detention centers. This action by the government has brought joy to countless families. Most of the Social Democrats released today had been detained since the uprising in February of this year, while many of the National Socialists had been imprisoned after the assassination of Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Vienna: The government issued an amnesty decree for Christmas, granting amnesty to all political prisoners arrested for participating in the Social Democratic uprising in February who have not yet been tried. Two thousand political prisoners were released from prison last week. In addition, President Miklas issued a pardon for 300 prisoners, including 170 political prisoners, of which 93 were Social Democrats and Communists and 77 were National Socialists. (Havas Telegram, 24th)

Berlin: The Berlin National Socialist Party held a Christmas children's reception in Mobit Street today, hosting 12,000 poor children. Long tables were arranged in the street, with gifts placed on them. Christmas trees were placed on both sides of the street to decorate the scene. Propaganda Minister Goebbels personally attended. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

New York: Many residents of major American cities are traveling during Christmas, so there have been many tragedies today. A train collision in Telaw, Wauhaiwo State, killed three people and injured fourteen. A plane crash in Walterburg, Tennessee, killed three people. A car collision in Lincoln, Nebraska, killed four people and injured five. In addition to the train and car accidents, a fire in a hotel in Carlsbad, New Mexico, killed three people and seriously injured five. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

Saarbrücken: Tomorrow is Christmas, and the Chairman of the Saar Administrative Commission, Knoxtert, has prepared packages containing clothes, shoes, toys, and food, and sent them to 2,050 poor children as Christmas gifts. (Havas Telegram, 24th)

Moscow: Anti-Christian movements have started again here and throughout Soviet Russia this Christmas. However, the slogans of this year's anti-religious movement seem to be milder than in previous years, merely stating, "Christmas is nothing more than an unconscious emotional reaction, and all educated workers should not participate." The anti-God movement is still the vanguard of the entire anti-Christian movement. Well-trained propaganda teams are making major efforts this year, using anti-religious films and speeches. There is no remote village that has not been touched by their presence. In addition, there are so-called anti-religious travel exhibitions, organized by members of countless anti-God groups. They adopt a more radical attitude and take the form of stormtroopers, making a great impact in Moscow and its suburbs. However, despite such enthusiastic anti-religious propaganda throughout the country, the annual Christmas holiday is still widely observed and celebrated by the people for a week, beginning today. (National Telegram, 24th)

Paris: On Thursday night, the German Ministry of Defense was heavily guarded, and the National Socialist Party was conducting a purge. It is estimated that no less than 3,000 people have been arrested and interrogated in the past three weeks. After this news arrived from Germany, newspapers here reprinted it, but they could not understand the reasons for the Ministry of Defense's lockdown and the purge. The newspapers also said, "Why have so many people been implicated in secret documents over the past three weeks? Is this action related to the will of Ernst, who was shot on June 30th?" The Morning Post stated, "Everyone in Germany is worried about what events will occur in Germany after the Saar vote on January 13th. Perhaps there will be some action to deal with the opposing forces of Protestantism, or perhaps the Special Task Force will be reorganized to reduce its power. All of this is unknown. In short, cabinet members are not leaving Berlin on Christmas Day, which shows that this holiday is extremely serious and of great importance." (Havas Telegram, 24th)

Internal Strife in Germany

The National Defense Force Considers Itself the Pillar of the State

The Party Army Is Not Content to Be Second

(Berlin) The German authorities, especially the National Defense Force, seem to be expressing considerable concern about the domestic political situation. Although officials have issued statements to reassure the public, the public's anxieties have not been allayed. Since the National Socialist Party's purge on June 30th, the National Defense Force has become the "military pillar of the Third Germany." Even Hitler himself has said this. However, the Party Army, the Stormtroopers, is not content to be second and is determined not to recognize that the National Socialist revolutionary movement has come to an end. As for the National Socialist Party's Security Force, it has risen to a prominent position since the June 30th incident and intends to consolidate its position. However, the National Defense Force aims to monopolize military power and will not allow the Security Force to act on its own. As a result, these three military organizations are engaged in internal strife. It is widely rumored that since the beginning of this month, the National Defense Force has taken various measures, such as canceling Christmas leave for soldiers. On Thursday evening, the area around the Ministry of Defense was heavily guarded, as if to prevent an incident from occurring. The uneasy attitude of the leaders of the National Defense Force is evident from this. In addition, the German political police are currently conducting a new purge, arresting large numbers of party members. Although officials are keeping silent about the number of arrests, it is estimated to be in the thousands. The reasons for the arrest of some party members are said to be related to morality, similar to what was seen during the June 30th incident. (Havas, 24th)

People of the Saar Trek Thousands of Miles to Vote from North and South America

Warmly Welcomed

Saarbrücken: Today, 350 people from the Saar returned from North and South America to participate in the plebiscite. The public welcomed them warmly, in stark contrast to their attitude towards the international forces. When they emerged from the station, cheers erupted, and they raised their arms in salute to the National Socialist Party. However, in accordance with the Saar Commission's ban, they did not display any flags. If they vote in favor of Germany on January 13th, their travel expenses will be reimbursed by local Saar organizations. The headquarters of the German Front violated the ban and displayed flags as usual. Last night, the police intervened and removed them. The lightest punishment for violating the order is three days of detention or a fine of 300 francs. Today, the last batch of Italian soldiers of the international forces also arrived, and the residents remained indifferent to them. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

Outlets for American Youth

(Washington) As of today, 100,000 unemployed American youth have joined the Civilian Conservation Corps in the mountains and forests. Another 68,210 will join between January 1st and 13th. (National Telegram, 23rd)

French Parliament Adjourns

Premier's Speech: Out with the Old, In with the New

Parliament and Government Trust Each Other

Respecting the Spirit of Republican Tradition

Both Houses Pass the Full Budget

(Paris) The order to adjourn Parliament has been announced in the Chamber of Deputies, thus ending the extraordinary session of Parliament for 1934. The regular session of Parliament for 1935 will begin on January 8th. Premier Flandin expressed his gratitude to the Chamber of Deputies at the opening, saying that the success of the government's proposed plans was largely due to the assistance of the Chamber. Speaker Bouisson also delivered a speech of thanks. It was not until 9:50 PM that the Premier read out the adjournment order. Before reading the adjournment order, Premier Flandin delivered a speech to the Chamber of Deputies, stating, "Parliament and the government trust each other. We are able to respect the spirit of republican tradition and to consider the supreme interests of the country. The people of the whole country can truly be comforted by this phenomenon as the end of the year approaches. Moreover, the restoration of normal economic activity depends entirely on the confidence of the people. Seeing the political situation as it is, a sense of trust will naturally arise. The government, on its part, will also have a sense of confidence as a result. From now on, we will be able to handle domestic and foreign affairs, as well as the problem of unemployment, with ease. After the opening of the regular session of Parliament in 1935, the government will meet with Parliament with various new bills in accordance with its announced policies. I hope you will provide assistance. As this year draws to a close, let us get rid of the old and bring in the new. We hope that, whether in domestic or international affairs, we can be guided by human sympathy, solidarity, and a desire for progress, to oppose war and eliminate human suffering," and so on. The Premier's speech was very well received by the members of Parliament.

After the full budget for 1935 was passed on its third reading by the Chamber of Deputies, it was also passed by the Senate. However, there were some points on which the Senate's views differed significantly from those of the Chamber. It was immediately sent back to the Chamber of Deputies, where it was passed on its fourth reading by a vote of 466 to 120.

It was then sent back to the Senate for review. Recently, the Senate reaffirmed its passage by a vote of 184 to 11. According to the budget, the expenditure portion is 47,817,011,976 francs, and the revenue portion is 46,991,968,737 francs. The difference between revenue and expenditure is a deficit of approximately 825,043,239 francs. In addition, the bill on clarifying the wheat market, after being slightly amended by the Chamber of Deputies, was passed. The amended provisions were accepted by the Senate Finance Committee and have recently been passed by the Senate. Furthermore, the Senate passed two other bills, one on the budget for the colony of Algeria, and the other stipulating that the Matignon Palace, the former site of the Austro-Hungarian Embassy before the European War, should be the office of the Prime Minister. Finally, the wine bill was discussed, and the two houses continued to discuss it until they agreed, before announcing the adjournment order. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

Simon Invites French Premier to Visit London

But Says It's Too Early

(Paris) British Foreign Secretary Simon went to Nice in the south of France to spend Christmas. On his way to Paris, he took the opportunity to meet with Foreign Minister Laval, as reported in yesterday's telegram. According to the Echo de Paris, Simon invited French Premier Flandin to visit London in January next year during the talks at the Foreign Ministry residence. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

(Paris) Following British Foreign Secretary Simon's discussions with Foreign Minister Laval here the day before yesterday on the issue of the League of Nations, there were rumors that Laval would soon be traveling to London. However, those responsible have denied this, saying that while it is highly likely that Laval will go to London, it will not happen in the short term, as he will be traveling to Rome to visit Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and is currently focusing on completing preliminary talks. (Havas dispatch, 20th)

America Takes a Calm Attitude, Japan Expresses Satisfaction

Britain Has Not Received American Cooperation Proposal

(Tokyo) The American government advised the American people on the 21st to avoid making provocative statements. The Japanese Foreign Ministry issued the following statement today regarding this issue. The Foreign Ministry has not yet received its official telegram. The actions of the American government are timely and

appropriate. Over the past year, the Foreign Ministry has been in contact with the Army, Navy, and Interior Ministry to avoid publishing belligerent or unfriendly articles or publications. In the current London preparatory talks, the Japanese representatives have not uttered a single provocative word. However, from across the Pacific, we often hear inflammatory statements, such as "If Japan abandons the Washington Treaty, the United States will strengthen the defense of the Pacific islands," "The United States is currently planning to build 40 warships," "If Japan builds three ships, the United States will build five," "Implement the strengthening of aircraft to deal with enemy submarines in the Pacific," and so on. Furthermore, Mr. Wien Sun's statement announcing the construction of the Nicaragua Canal is extremely provocative to the feelings of the Japanese people. Now that the London preparatory talks are about to be finalized, all responsible persons should be careful in making statements. The American representatives' remarks to journalists on the night of the 20th caused the Japanese public to feel extremely unpleasant. The Japanese sincerely welcome the American government's recent ban on general provocative statements. (United Press dispatch, 24th)

(London) According to American newspapers, the US State Department is currently drafting a naval agreement between Britain and the United States. Regarding this matter, well-informed British sources stated that they have not received any formal information from Washington to prove that this news is accurate, and that any draft naval agreement between the two sides, or a plan to establish a united front, is definitely not something that Britain can endorse. The goal of the London Naval Conference was originally to study whether a general naval treaty could be extended or amended. Therefore, what Britain is striving for in the naval field is only to conclude a general agreement, and nothing else is known. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

(London) According to the Daily Mail, the British government is now planning to find a way to bring representatives of the naval powers together again in London next spring to discuss. According to the British, the aim of the recent attempt was to obtain a method agreed upon by all countries for monitoring naval armaments in the future. Britain maintains its original position that all naval shipbuilding plans must be publicly announced. Foreign Secretary Simon is currently spending the Christmas holiday in Cannes, France. Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira will visit him after his return to discuss the matter. (Associated Press dispatch, 24th)

(Paris) Le Matin reported that, after the news of Japan's announcement to abolish the Washington Naval Treaty was confirmed, Washington and London immediately exchanged views. American Ambassador to Britain Bingham has now returned home. Upon his arrival in Washington, he discussed with Secretary of State Hull for two hours. The American government also clearly expressed the outline of the policies it should adopt in future negotiations yesterday afternoon, divided into six points: (1) Adopt a cautious attitude to avoid stimulating Japanese nationalism; (2) Britain and the United States should cooperate closely on all issues in the Far East; (3) This cooperation should also be used to resist Japan's demand for naval equality; (4) The United States will build warships so that its naval strength can reach the limits permitted by the current naval treaty; (5) The results of negotiations between Britain and the United States on cooperation should be kept secret from both the press and the public; (6) Continue diplomatic negotiations with Japan to find a way to maintain the current 5:5:3 ratio. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

(Paris) Le Journal's foreign edition published an article by the renowned journalist Saint-Brice on the Washington Naval Treaty, saying that if the Washington Naval Treaty continued to exist, according to the ratio stipulated in the treaty, Britain and the United States could build 90,000 tons of navy each year, Japan could build 55,000 tons, and France and Italy could each build 40,000 tons. The British navy has already been reduced to the minimum limit below which it cannot be dispensed with, and now it cannot accept the general reduction of naval tonnage by various countries. Its attitude is strange. The article concluded that if the political competition among the powers does not disappear, then all negotiations on armament issues will not easily produce results. The failure of the Washington Treaty and the collapse of the London Naval Conference are all due to this. It is hoped that lessons will be learned from this, and that it will be known that political issues are important, then it may be possible. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

Dollar Devaluation Issue

Roosevelt Refuses to Continue Inflation

(Washington) Senator Thomas told the Associated Press today that the issue of dollar devaluation will be the most important point of contention in the next Congress. However, the forces opposing further devaluation by the government are also gradually developing. It is said that the Treasury Department and the Federal Reserve Board are currently drafting legislation to consolidate political control over the Federal Reserve System. This move will further advance the government's political control over bank lending. Some experts believe that the government can therefore raise prices, lower the value of currency, and reduce the national debt. (National Electric, 23rd)

(Washington) President Roosevelt and New Deal congressmen have decided to oppose inflation and veterans' bonus bills, but will compromise on the 30-hour work week demanded by labor unions. It is said that President Roosevelt has already rejected the bonus bill and has not formally expressed opposition to continued inflation. American Veterans Association President Bergeruno declared that he will submit a bonus bill when Congress convenes, estimating that approximately $2,000,000,000 to $200,000,000,000 in cash will be paid out immediately in veterans' bonus bonds. (National Electric, 23rd)

Turkish Parliament Dissolved

Legislative Elections Held Early

Ankara The Parliament has been declared dissolved, and its legislative work has come to an end. According to the current Turkish constitution, the dissolution of Parliament can only be decided by a two-thirds majority of itself. Prime Minister İsmet İnönü declared on November 15 of the third year that the legislative elections would be held earlier this winter to consolidate the position of the People's Party and the current government after the elections. Recently, the Parliament declared its own dissolution, which is the basis for holding legislative elections early. (Havas dispatch, 24th)

The representatives are scheduled to go to the Executive Yuan on the 25th to petition and entertain reporters. It is heard that after receiving the complaint, the Ministry of Education immediately ordered He to reply. He replied to the Ministry of Education a few days ago that the provincial government did not issue study abroad funds when it was in Tai'an, and that forming factions for personal gain was even more untrue. Japan's Railway Policy in "Manchukuo"

The Beihei-Chenggong-Tumen Line Opens

Three Additional Lines Planned, Including Mishan Line

Soviet Union Responds with Railway Policy

The South Manchuria Railway Company is directly responsible for guiding the "Manchukuo" railway policy, which has been gradually implemented since last year. To date, two major lines have achieved results:

(1) The northern end of the Huhai Railway, a railway from Bei'an Town via Chenqing and Aigun to Daheihe, was completed on December 14th. The track laying work was completed, and the first full-line test run began on the same day.

(2) The line from the Tumen River bank terminus of the Jihui Railway, via Lishugou and Ning'an, crossing the Chinese Eastern Railway at Mudanjiang, to Ningbei, is also gradually being completed. It has now begun temporary operations.

The Beihei Line is an extension of the Huhai Line and the Qitao and Sitao Lines. From an economic perspective, it will completely control the production of the Heilongjiang Plain in the future. Both agricultural and forest products will be absorbed by this line. Before this line was open, it would take a week to travel by boat from Harbin to Daheihe in the summer. Now, it only takes twenty hours. It can also connect with the Jihui Line via the Harbin-Lafa Railway and depart from the North Korean port of Chongjin, which is more convenient and faster than going to Dalian via the South Manchuria Railway. It also surpasses part of the benefits of the Chinese Eastern Railway.

From a military perspective, everyone recognizes that Daheihe, facing the Heilongjiang River and backed by the Lesser Khingan Mountains, is a future key point in Japanese-Soviet military affairs. On the Japanese side, if the Red Army is allowed to cross the river from here and cross the Lesser Khingan Mountains, then the entire Heilongjiang province will not be secure, and "North Manchuria" will inevitably be seized. On the contrary, if Japan crosses the river from Daheihe, seizes Hailanpao, and cuts off the connection between Vladivostok and Chita, then the coastal province and northern Sakhalin Island will be under Japanese control. Therefore, it is actively completing this railway. In the event of an emergency, it can connect with Daheihe from the South Manchuria Railway via the Sitao and Qitao lines, and on the other hand, it can land from Chongjin, go through Dunhua, Lafa, Harbin, and Hulan, and head north. From this, we can see how important this line is.

Although the line from the Tumen River bank to Ningbei is only 250 kilometers long, it passes through the prosperous areas of eastern "Manchukuo." Even in its current undeveloped state, the accumulated goods along the line (grains and forest products) are over 100,000 tons. Therefore, this is a nurturing line for the newly opened ports in northern Korea. In the future, when the port is opened, the land there will be developed, and the economic benefits will be more than ten times what they are today. Moreover, this line will soon be extended to Yilan (the central area for Japanese immigration to "Manchukuo"), absorbing the agricultural production along the Songhua River. The mission of the former Chinese Eastern Railway will probably be reduced by half, and the convenience of Japanese immigration will be further increased. After transportation becomes more convenient, perhaps the transplanted farmers will no longer flee back to Japan. Although its military significance is not as great as that of the Beihei Line, its role in cutting off the Chinese Eastern Railway and controlling eastern Jilin is not small.

This December, it is planning to invest another 40 million Japanese yen to start building three lines: Mishan to Linkou, Solun to Tuquan, and Ripingjie to Si'an County (under Liaoning, formerly known as Dageta). The last line has considerable economic significance, but the military connection is not very significant. However, the first two lines are important locations. Mishan is an important town in eastern Jilin, and Solun is a key point in the southern part of the Greater Khingan Mountains. Such an arrangement not only has a passive defensive meaning, but especially the Solun-Tuquan line, will naturally connect with the Sitao line. Its extension into Outer Mongolia is also anticipated. Therefore, although the Soviet Union is willing to sell the Chinese Eastern Railway in the hope of exchanging it for peace, it also knows that this is unreliable. At the same time, the radical public opinion in Japan advocates that if the Soviet Union wants peace, it must withdraw from Eastern Siberia and Outer Mongolia and be controlled by Japan to avoid conflict. The Soviet Union must be vigilant in this regard. Therefore, in addition to its Second Five-Year Plan, it has the following important railway plans: (1) Building a new Siberian Transcontinental Railway as a second transportation line in case the eastern line of the Siberian Railway cannot be used; (2) The Siberian Grand Railway, originally a single-track railway, can no longer fulfill the task of promoting its national industrialization, and is particularly inconvenient militarily. Therefore, double-track railways will be laid in the future to facilitate traffic; (3) All areas bordering northern "Manchukuo" will be sensitive to Japan's aggressive railway policy. Consequently, the construction of a dense railway network within Soviet territory, goes without saying, is heavily military in nature. From the railway policies of both sides, it can be seen that their wartime preparations are still very active. (December 18th, Dalian)

Security Issues in the War Zone

Bandit Troubles Need to be Eliminated Urgently

Peiping Correspondence: Security issues in the war zone have not yet been resolved. The crux of the problem lies in two points: (1) Disputes over the number of personnel and firearms in the newly formed security teams; (2) The reorganization of the security teams and the problem of suppressing the remnants of bandits. It is undeniable that the security teams in the war zone were formed temporarily during the recovery of the war zone, and those recruited had been temporarily enlisted. The command is not unified, and the training has not been perfected. In addition, the strength is insufficient, so it cannot be suppressed on a large scale. Therefore, problems arise frequently. Unless the reorganization is strengthened and the strength is increased to eliminate the remnants of bandits and block all ports to eliminate the source of chaos, the security of the war zone cannot be discussed. The authorities are aware of this and are training new security teams on the one hand and stipulating fundamental solutions on the other hand. However, the Japanese are picky about this matter in many ways, and it has not been realized. The number of security teams stationed within the war zone can reach 9,000 according to the Tanggu Agreement, and there is no restriction on the weapons they carry. However, the Japanese, regardless of the agreement, have always insisted that the number of personnel should not exceed 6,000, and in addition to rifles, not to mention artillery, even machine guns are prohibited from being carried. This has led to the inability of the newly formed security teams to enter the war zone, and the security problem cannot be resolved. Recently, conflicts have broken out again between the Yutian Security Team and the militia, and the local area has been ravaged again. The authorities are urgently seeking a thorough solution in order to achieve lasting results. On the one hand, they are mediating the disputes between the teams to address the symptoms, and on the other hand, they are engaging in earnest negotiations with the Japanese to address the root causes. The War Zone Clearing Committee is working hard and has been in contact with Chai Shan, the military attaché of the Japanese Embassy, ​​through Zhu Shiqin, Yin Tong, and Yin Rugeng. A meeting was held the day before yesterday, but there was no significant result. Yesterday, Zhu Shiqin went to Tianjin from Peiping to visit Yu Xuezhong to negotiate everything. The two sides in Yutian are still confronting each other, and the situation is serious and needs to be resolved urgently. After Zhu's consultation with Yu in Tianjin, he will transfer to Tangshan and go to Yutian to first seek a temporary end to the current dispute. The fundamental issue will then be addressed in Peiping with representatives from the Japanese side to find a fair solution. Chai Shan went to Tianjin yesterday to discuss a certain issue. At 6 pm today, he and Yoshida, the Japanese foreign affairs commissioner who transferred from Changchun via the west, arrived in Peiping to negotiate.

(22nd)

Implementing Standard Pricing in Beiping

Trial Implementation Achieves Excellent Results

Elimination of Unsavory Business Practices Foreseeable

The Beiping Branch of the National Goods Bank of China and the Beiping Municipal Government, in a recent effort to promote the increasing prosperity of commerce in Beiping, have resolved to decisively eradicate the unsavory practice of haggling prices among various shops. The initial reform measure involves the implementation of standard market prices. Starting on the first of this month, a trial implementation was conducted at the Dong'an Market, yielding excellent results. Subsequently, on the sixteenth of this month, it was extended to the Xidan Market. It is now learned that starting from New Year's Day next year, all shops city-wide will uniformly adopt standard pricing. Details of the implementation process and its benefits are recorded below:

Motivation for Implementation　In Beiping, for shop-front transactions, prior to a decade ago, the virtue of "no second price" was still upheld. Instances of deviation were few, and even then, limited to stall vendors, who, operating on small capital, sought only to move their goods for quicker turnover. The hardships they faced were well-known to seasoned observers, thus patrons sometimes felt they got a "bad deal" or a "bargain." In other words, those unafraid to put in the effort to haggle repeatedly could secure a better price. Those who paid the asking price honestly invariably felt they were overcharged. In recent years, due to the economic downturn, shops of all sizes, striving to survive, sought to "snatch business" while ensuring they did not lose money. Thus, the practice of "cheap sales" flourished. As long as someone entered their shop, they were determined not to let them leave empty-handed. As competition intensified, the mercantile ethics of "no second price" were completely abandoned. The municipal authorities believe that such "commercial warfare" not only affects the prosperity of the market but also leads to the further decline of merchants' morals. Furthermore, the incident of a certain celebrity being deceived when buying antique porcelain bottles at the Dong'an Market led to the consideration of rescue measures. The Dong'an Market was the first to implement standard pricing, motivated by these concerns. The outcome has been excellent.

Results of Standard Pricing　The determination of standard prices seemed superficially difficult, and whether the shops could faithfully adhere to them was a matter of concern for many. The implementation method involved the shops forming a price evaluation committee, based on incoming invoices, to set prices for each item. Once assessed and labeled, the prices could not be arbitrarily raised or lowered. Recognizing the pain of past deceptive practices to attract customers, the merchants also believed that this method was necessary to maintain the status quo. As a result, since the implementation of standard market prices at the Dong'an Market, business has generally improved. Goods that previously yielded only a 2% profit margin can now be sold for 3% or 4%. Shop A no longer needs to drastically cut prices, and Shop B no longer needs to make significant sacrifices. Even antique stalls, which previously had no standard prices, now offer no discounts, adhering to a uniform price. In the past, the average daily sales for the entire Dong'an Market were approximately 34,000 yuan. Since the implementation of standard pricing, the average daily sales have increased to over 51,000 yuan. Since its implementation in the Xidan Market on the sixteenth of this month, business at the various shops has also shown improvement.

Fundamental Strategy for Prosperity　According to Cai Yuan, the Director of the Beiping Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Beiping is a famous former capital, and its cultural development is unparalleled in the world. Each year, numerous tourist groups, both large and small, from various countries visit Beiping, along with countless individual tourists. When visiting Beiping, they invariably purchase large quantities of goods to take back to their countries as souvenirs. If merchants treat them dishonestly, it will inevitably affect the prosperity of the entire commercial sector. Mayor Yuan, recognizing this, instructed the bureau to establish a standard pricing system to alleviate customers' suspicions and the hassle of haggling, while also ensuring that merchants' legitimate profits are not sacrificed by false cheap sales and giveaways. The municipal government is actively planning the construction of cultural and tourist areas in Beiping. When these projects are completed, tourists from various countries visiting Beiping will undoubtedly feel at home. This will aid the restoration of the former capital. (22nd)

Bandit Leader Gao Shaobai Killed in Southern Fujian

Three Kidnapped Victims Rescued on the Spot

Two Women and Children Killed by Stray Bullets

Xiamen Dispatch: Gao Shaobai, a notorious bandit in southern Fujian, was the younger brother of Shang Weiguo, who was previously executed by the provincial government. After Shang Weiguo's execution, Gao Shaobai continued to operate as a bandit from his old lair in Fushan. During the Fujian Rebellion, when the anti-rebellion army arose, Gao gathered his men and requested to be incorporated into the army. However, due to his incorrigible bandit nature, he was subsequently attacked by the army. Eventually, Gao Wuchi led the remaining men to surrender. Gao Shaobai disagreed with Wuchi and remained in his old lair, joining forces with Wang Chengfa and other bandits from western Hui'an, continuing his outlaw life. The area north of Quanzhou's North Gate, including Jinbei, was frequently harassed. Lu Pengqi, the town head and militia commander of the eastern part of the first district of Jinjiang County, believed that Gao Shaobai had no intention of surrendering and that Wan Wai, a resident of Xiaotian Village in his district, had been kidnapped by him and a ransom of 500 yuan demanded. He, therefore, sought and received approval from the county government to thoroughly eliminate them regardless of jurisdictional boundaries. On the evening of the 18th, at approximately 8:00 PM, Lu dispatched 100 militia members in cars, traveling along the Quanluo Road and then turning onto Shuangyang Road, resting in Xingnei Village. At approximately 2:00 AM on the 19th, they set off in four groups, and at approximately 3:00 AM, they entered Fushan, splitting into three groups to attack the residences of Gao Shaobai, Wang Chengfa, and Ji Zhuzai. Another team was assigned to guard the location where the kidnapped victims were held. It was agreed that the attack would commence at Gao's residence first, and then the other three groups would simultaneously open fire. The group attacking Gao's residence initiated the attack. After breaching the gate, gunfire erupted from inside the house. The militia members charged into the house, and Gao Shaobai and his nephew Ji Haoyin, along with three others, were killed inside. Ji Zhuzai and four others in another group were also killed at their residence. Wang Chengfa escaped. Three kidnapped victims were rescued. Two women and children were killed by stray bullets. Lu and others then brought the rescued victims to the city to report the case. County Magistrate Yu Gongwu highly praised the members of each team. Over the years, more than a dozen bandit leaders in southern Fujian have been killed. After the central army entered Fujian, Lin Jing and You Sifu were also killed. Now, Gao Shaobai has been put to death. It is hoped that the bandits who have plagued Fujian Province for over a decade can now be eliminated. (21st)

Huihua Steamboat of Xiamen Capsizes

Forty-Six People Rescued

Two Bodies Recovered

Xiamen Dispatch: The Huihua steamboat of the Yonghe Shipping Company of this city departed from Xiamen at 2:00 PM on the 18th, carrying cargo to Shima Town in Zhangzhou. While passing Chicken Island near Wooden Island, it capsized due to strong winds. As of the evening of the 20th, it was learned that 46 crew members and passengers had been rescued. The number of deaths and missing persons is unknown due to the unclear number of passengers on board. The losses are estimated at over 20,000 yuan. Details are as follows:

According to a survivor named Guo, the ship carried over 70 passengers and a large amount of cargo on that day. There were 180 barrels of oil at the front of the ship, and much of the other cargo was placed on the deck. Due to insufficient seating, many passengers were lying down or scattered on the cargo boxes. The ship was thus top-heavy. While passing through the Chicken Island entrance and turning towards Haimen, where the currents from Shima and Fugong Harbor meet to form a strong confluence, the waves were extremely large. At the same time, a strong southeasterly wind was blowing, causing the ship to rock violently. After tilting severely several times to the left and right, a gust of wind caused the ship to lose its balance and capsize to the left, eventually turning over completely with its hull facing upwards. The cargo immediately fell into the sea. Approximately 80 passengers and crew members clung to the hull as the ship capsized slowly, preventing them from being swept away by the waves. Shortly after the capsizing, a Meijiang boat passed by, and the survivors cried out for help. The Meijiang boat circled once, but due to the strong wind and waves, the passengers on the Meijiang boat, fearing the small size and danger of their vessel, prevented them from approaching. It then sailed directly to Xiamen. Subsequently, two sailing boats arrived and rescued 35 people, taking them to Shima and Haimen. Guo (the survivor) and five of his friends were among them. It is estimated that approximately 40 people drowned or went missing. The above is the account of the Huihua's accident. After the Meijiang arrived in Xiamen and reported the incident, the Yonghe Shipping Company immediately dispatched two steamboats, and the water police dispatched the Haiping ship to assist. When they arrived at the scene, it was already 8:00 PM at night. All the survivors had already been rescued, and only the Huihua's hull was visible, floating upside down. The rescue boats then returned. The next morning, on the 19th, they returned to tow the capsized Huihua back. The bodies of an elderly woman in her 70s and a three-year-old child were found in the hull. The search for bodies on that day yielded no results. On the 20th, three steamboats and more than ten small boats continued the search for bodies, but still found nothing. The incident has caused an uproar in Xiamen. It is considered as serious as the sinking of the Bianli ship in 1930, which resulted in over 150 deaths. The Longxi Native Place Association immediately held a meeting and established a registry for the families of the deceased to investigate the number of victims. The Silk Industry Guild sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, criticizing the shipping company for prioritizing profits over safety and disregarding the lives of merchants and millions of dollars worth of goods, requesting serious negotiations. According to the Yonghe Shipping Company's report to the customs, the ship carried 51 pieces of miscellaneous goods and textiles, 180 barrels of raw oil, 31 passengers, and 17 crew members. The customs had inspected and approved the manifest, and the Second Brigade of the water police had also approved the voyage. The customs had set the passenger limit for the Huihua at 80 people and the weight limit at 9.75 tons. The passengers and cargo carried on this voyage did not exceed these limits. Furthermore, the Huihua's inspection period had expired, and the entire ship had been repaired in Shima before reporting to the Xiamen Maritime Affairs Office of the Ministry of Transportation for inspection, which approved the voyage. It also had 60 life jackets and 3 lifebuoys. The safety equipment was also in good order. This incident was due to the strong wind and waves, a natural disaster that could not be prevented by human effort. However, according to passengers, there were over 70 passengers, and nearly 90 people including crew members. Furthermore, according to a letter from the Silk Fabric Guild to the Chamber of Commerce, the ship was carrying 168 loads of cargo, approximately 10 tons, according to known estimates from various shops. Therefore, the responsibility is currently unclear and depends on whether more bodies are discovered and the results of the registration of the families of the deceased. Furthermore, much of the cargo entrusted by Yongkangcheng and others was retrieved by local villagers after the ship capsized. The water police dispatched patrol boats to the nearby villages on the 20th to recover the goods and continue searching for bodies. (21st)

Ten Counties in Jiangxi Conscript Labor to Dredge the Fu River

Construction to Begin on January 16th Next Year, Completion in Twenty Days

Nanchang Dispatch: The Construction Department of the provincial government, recognizing that the rivers of Jiangxi Province have been neglected for years, resulting in the growth of islands, divergent river channels, and a desolate appearance, with the Fu River being the worst affected, realizes that the river lacks the capacity to discharge floodwaters, causing frequent flooding. In terms of navigation, the water depth in winter is often less than one meter, making it difficult for lightly loaded sailboats to navigate. The river brings only water disasters without its benefits. Now that banditry has been suppressed, renovation and dredging are the most urgent tasks for future construction. It has been decided to start with the Fu River basin this winter, following Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's decree of the people's service, by conscripting labor each winter to carry out various water conservancy projects, progressing annually to eliminate water disasters and promote water conservancy, thereby benefiting the people's livelihood and the national economy. The plan has been approved by the provincial government meeting today (21st). Yan Fangtian, the director of the Water Conservancy Bureau, will soon go to the various counties to urge implementation. Construction is scheduled to begin on January 16th next year and be completed within twenty clear days. Inspection and acceptance will be completed by February 16th. The plan is appended below:

Engineering Standards　The main problems of the Fu River are the growth of islands and divergent channels at medium water levels, and unstable embankments and overflowing floods at high water levels. The river's ability to scour sand is greatest during high water levels. At medium water levels, the river has no fixed channels, causing the water to disperse and deposit silt, forming islands and obstructing the river. Therefore, this year's projects will focus on the following two aspects: (A) Dredging islands and shoals downstream from Nanfeng. Dredge the islands and shoals that obstruct the flow of water at medium water levels, selecting key areas. The dredging depth should be such that the bottom of the new channel is level with the low water surface. The width should be based on the width of the river channel at medium water levels in nearby good river sections. The slope of the bank away from the water on the new river channel should be a gentle slope of 1:10 to 1:20. The dredged sand should be used to reinforce the embankments on both sides or to fill in the beaches on both sides. If the newly filled sand is easily eroded by the water flow, it should be covered with solid soil on the water side or surrounded by embankments to prevent erosion. (B) Reinforcing the embankments along both sides of the river downstream from Linchuan. The standard for the embankments should be a top width of 3 meters, 1 meter higher than the highest flood level, an outer slope of at least 1:1.5, and an inner slope of 1:2. However, for non-direct impact embankment sections, if the project is too large, the inner slope may be changed to two types of slopes: from the top of the embankment to two-thirds of the height, use a slope of 1:1, and from two-thirds of the height to the foot of the embankment, use a slope of 1:2. All ditches and ports caused by embankment breaches should be properly blocked.

Construction Sections　The construction sections planned for this year are as follows: (1) Dredging the Shuinan to Dougang section in Nanfeng. (2) Dredging the Jixianli to Qiufang section in Lichuan. (3) Dredging the Taipingqiao to Yangjiadu section in Nancheng. (4) Dredging the Guanhongqiao to Tanfang section in Yihuang. (5) Dredging the section in front of the Yuhun Temple in Chongren. (6) Dredging the area from Huwan to Xiamashan in Jinxi. (7) Constructing embankments along the Fu River in Linchuan and blocking the breaches on both sides. (8) Dredging the Nanbeiqiao to Yangfang section in Dongxiang. (9) Dredging the Shun Port project in both Nanjin counties and repairing various dike embankments in Jinxian. (10) Repairing and reinforcing the embankments along the river in Nanchang and dredging the Shun Port project in both Nanjin counties. The above proposed construction sections for each county will be resurveyed by personnel from the Water Conservancy Bureau, and construction will be carried out.

Number of Workers Conscripted　The number of workers to be conscripted this year is determined according to the number of able-bodied men and the severity of the famine in each county. The proposed number of workers to be conscripted from each county is as follows: (1) Nanfeng: 2,000 people. (2) Lichuan: 2,000 people. (3) Nancheng: 3,000 people. (4) Yihuang: 4,000 people. (5) Chongren: 5,000 people. (6) Jinxi: 3,000 people. (7) Linchuan: 20,000 people. (8) Dongxiang: 5,000 people. (9) Jinxian: 6,000 people. (10) Nanchang: 20,000 people. In total, 70,000 workers will be conscripted daily from the above counties. The county magistrates of each county are responsible for collecting the workers and supervising the implementation of the construction methods stipulated by the Water Conservancy Bureau.

Medical Students in Nantong Involved in Corpse Desecration Case

Yan Jialiu, Sha Chonggui, Wang Shikuang, Huang Yi, Chen Dan, and other five students of the second year of the medical department of Nantong College, excavated graves in the South Yizhong of the public sports field in the south of the city, picking up bones to make human skeleton specimens. It aroused public anger. The village chief, Sun Pengnian, reported to the Public Security Bureau, which sent the five students and the retrieved skeletons to the court. After interrogation by Chief Prosecutor Liu Shizhu, the five students were released on bail by the school. The investigation has now concluded. Yan Jialiu and others have been publicly prosecuted for the crime of corpse desecration. The Criminal Court has scheduled a public hearing on the 26th by Judge Sheng Shengxiu.

Si Guishan, a poultry farmer from Renjiakou, gave his daughter, Wu Nuo, in marriage to Zhang Miancai a few days ago. However, one day after returning to her in-laws' home, her husband suddenly reported her death. Si Guishan reported the matter to the court's prosecutor for inspection. Extortion in Haimen Leads to Death

Xu Xinggen, a farmer near Yongchang Town in the Fifth District, had an argument with his wife, Zhang, last month and went to the Huang Fuzai teahouse in the town for mediation. As a result, Xu acknowledged and paid 1,300-1,400 cash as tea fees. The other day, Huang Fuzai demanded 3,000 cash from Xu for expenses. Xu was temporarily unable to pay. However, Huang acted aggressively and confined Xu in the teahouse. After mediation by bystanders, Xu was given three days to pay before being released. Xu was stimulated by this incident, feeling extremely resentful, and had the idea of ending his life. He went to the Pincheng Hall pharmacy in the town, purchased a package of arsenic, and secretly swallowed it after returning home. He died of poisoning that night. Yesterday, the family of the deceased requested the county government to send personnel to inspect the body. The district public office has detained Huang Fuzai and sent him to the county government for interrogation.

Marital Quarrel Leads to Tragedy

Dai Hongxiu, a villager from Zhonggong Township in the First District of Qidong, married Shi, who was very fierce. Quarrels often occurred between the couple. The other day, due to a trivial argument, Shi, disregarding the consequences, grabbed a kitchen knife and slashed Hongxiu's head, causing blood to flow like a river, and he fell to the ground. Shi, realizing she had caused a disaster, fled without a trace. After being discovered by neighbors, she was rescued and resuscitated. However, her injuries were severe and her life may be in danger.

Unfilial Son in Jiashan Beats His Eighty-Year-Old Mother

Qiu Ziqing, also known as Lanxing, a resident of Qiaohutong Street in Tianning Town, married Ni. His elderly mother is over eighty years old and has a history of mental illness. On the 18th, she had an argument with her daughter-in-law, which led to a conflict. Qiu Ziqing and his wife, Ni, tied up their mother's hands and feet and beat her with fists and kicks, injuring her head and causing blood to flow continuously, and her body was covered in bruises. Her life was in danger. Neighbors reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau, who arrested the unfilial son for interrogation.
