Promoters of the "Student National Goods Year" Held a Preparatory Meeting Yesterday

Elected Staff, Approved Organizational Outline, etc.

And Agreed to Hold an Opening Ceremony on New Year's Day

Various circles in this city have designated next year as "Student National Goods Year." Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the association held a promoters' meeting at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA to approve the organizational and work outlines and elect directors. Details are as follows:

Chairman's Report: Chairman Pan Gongzhan reported, "The preparatory committee for the 'Student National Goods Year' invited gentlemen to participate as members, and we are honored by their enthusiastic participation. The significance of this initiative lies in the fact that the National Goods Year movement has been ongoing for two years. In these two years, it has achieved considerable success. The general public believes that the trade deficit is very large, considering the promoters ineffective and unproductive. Some say that imports of women's cosmetics have not decreased, and the promotion by women's circles has also been ineffective. However, conversely, if we had not promoted it, the import volume might have been even greater. Therefore, the failure to reduce the trade deficit cannot be blamed on the ineffectiveness of the promoters. It should be understood that there are many new foreign products, which are overwhelming and beyond our expectations. For example, with the accessibility of highways, the number of cars and gasoline consumption is increasing daily, which is beyond the ability of promoters to control. The increase in imported cosmetics is not entirely used by our country's women; some may be used by foreigners. At the same time, it is also related to social customs and habits, such as the increase in dance halls and cafes, which leads to more cosmetics consumption. This is related to social education. From our own perspective, doing something is better than doing nothing, and putting in effort is better than not putting in effort. If we want to increase exports, we must continue to work hard. We firmly believe that in these two years, the social mentality of looking down on domestic goods has decreased, and the sales of foreign goods versus domestic goods are better for domestic goods. The failure of domestic goods emporiums in the past has gradually diminished over the past two years, and they have been able to stand on their own. This is also an undeniable fact. Although it is due to the factories' own improvements, the change in social attitudes is a major reason. The National Goods movement should promote mutual progress between consumption, production, and sales. Why do we focus on students? Because students have pure minds and can set an example to awaken the general public, their achievements will be greater than others. Therefore, we have designated next year as 'Student National Goods Year' and will intensify our work. Looking back at the student movements of 1915, 1919, 1925, and 1931, anti-Japanese and anti-Japanese boycotts were all primarily led by students, and it may be more effective to unite with industry and commerce to promote domestic goods." Chen Jicheng and Zhang Shouyong then reported (omitted).

Resolutions: The discussion of proposals began immediately. (1) Decision on the name: It was resolved to name it "Student National Goods Year Promotion Federation." (2) Decision on the organizational outline: It was resolved to pass it. (3) Decision on the work outline: It was resolved to pass it. (4) Election of directors: It was resolved to elect them on the spot. (5) Election of conveners of the board of directors: It was resolved to nominate Pan Gongzhan, Yu Zuoting, Wu Zhihao, Zhang Shouyong, and Fang Yexian. (6) Decision on the New Year's Day opening ceremony: It was resolved to hand it over to the preparatory committee. (7) Fundraising: It was resolved to ask Fang Yexian and Wu Zhihao to advance funds. Organizational Outline: The organizational outline passed is as follows: (1) This association is jointly initiated by educational and commercial groups. Based on this year's National Goods Movement year, it is named "Student National Goods Year Promotion Federation." (2) The purpose of this association is to promote the inherent patriotic spirit of students, awaken the public to use domestic goods, and unite with industry and commerce to promote the National Goods Movement. (3) The members of this association are schools, domestic goods factories, domestic goods stores, and groups enthusiastic about domestic goods. All those who join this association shall send one or two representatives. (4) The membership fee of this association shall be freely contributed by each member. (5) This association shall have a board of directors, and the directors shall be publicly elected by the initiating groups. The board of directors shall decide to appoint members from the nominated representatives to form the following committees: 1. School Committee, 2. Domestic Goods Factory Committee, 3. Domestic Goods Store Committee, 4. Economic Committee, 5. Design Committee, 6. Publicity Committee. (6) The School Committee may establish branches in each school. (7) This association may hire staff as needed to serve each committee under the direction of the board of directors. (8) The rules and regulations for the board of directors and each committee shall be established separately. (9) Matters not covered in this outline may be added, deleted, or modified by the board of directors.

Work Outline: The work outline, after deliberation, is as follows: (1) Realize the objectives of the "Student National Goods Year." (2) Assist school members in holding publicity gatherings. (3) Assist domestic goods factories in improving product quality and increasing production quantity. (4) Assist domestic goods stores in promoting domestic goods. (5) Assist each member in establishing domestic goods promotion agencies. (6) Report monthly to each member on the monthly trade deficit situation of the customs and compare it with the same month last year.

Banking Sector Offers Advice, Asking the Ministry of Finance to Reward Silver Imports

Refund Original Taxes or Exempt Future Taxes When Returning

Foreign Banks Have Requested the Ministry of Finance to Consider

Minister Kong Declares That He Will Never Allow Inflation

New Voice News reports: The Shanghai money market is extremely tight, and the daily interest rate has risen to four jiao. The reason is that the autumn harvest of agricultural products and year-end accounting have led to a shortage of silver. In addition to strict crackdowns by customs on smuggling, the Ministry of Finance has promulgated reward and punishment measures, strictly ordering provinces and industries to assist. Although its effectiveness is significant, it is not a fundamental solution. A New Voice News reporter learned yesterday from the Shanghai banking sector that banking leaders Zhang Gongquan, Chen Guangfu, and others had visited Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi to offer advice on rewarding silver imports. Because China's silver only has exports and no imports, although exports have been greatly reduced, if this continues, China's silver will inevitably gradually decrease in the future. It is hoped that the government will find ways to reward silver exports. However, the bank's view is that, for example, when exported silver is returned, the silver tax and equalization tax levied at the time of export by customs should be refunded, or when the returned silver is re-exported in the future, export tax and equalization tax should be exempted. At the same time, in view of market rumors of inflation, it is requested that Minister Kong make a clear statement to dispel public doubts and reassure people. At that time, Minister Kong promised to consider rewarding silver imports, but strongly refuted the rumors of inflation and solemnly declared that as long as he is in office, he will never allow inflation, reduce the silver content of silver coins, or issue inconvertible banknotes. It is even more absurd. It is heard that foreign banks such as HSBC and Mercantile have requested the Ministry of Finance to consider not levying taxes again when silver that has already been levied with export silver tax and equalization tax is re-exported after being returned. The Ministry of Finance is considering this issue. If approved, the silver previously shipped by HSBC and other foreign banks to Hong Kong and other places will be shipped back to regulate finance, because the number of foreign banks exporting is very large, resulting in thin inventories. In case of a bank run, it would be difficult to cope, so for precautionary purposes, they are willing to ship back the exported silver.

Minister Kong Cables Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to Strictly Suppress the Smuggling of Silver Exports

Three Stipulated Reward and Punishment Measures

Please Order Military and Police Agencies to Comply

Dagong News reports: In order to prevent the outflow of cash and stabilize domestic silver prices, the Ministry of Finance has implemented the levying of export tax and equalization tax on silver, but there are still a few unscrupulous people who seek profits through smuggling. Although the customs have been strictly investigating, they have not been completely eliminated. Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi convened many experts and held several meetings with the banking sector to formulate reward and punishment measures, which will be implemented immediately, and cabled Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to instruct the military and police agencies to comply. The content of the measures is extremely thorough. After implementation, smuggling can be eliminated. The original text of Kong's telegram to Chiang and the implemented reward and punishment measures are as follows:

Telegram to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek: Chairman Chiang, in view of the fact that the silver export tax was originally intended to stabilize finance and the market, there are unscrupulous people who seek private gain, disregard the overall situation, and frequently smuggle exports. Violating the law and operating privately is extremely hateful. The Ministry has previously strictly ordered all customs houses to investigate carefully and ordered silver and money industry guilds and chambers of commerce to jointly supervise and secretly report. In order to prevent and control thoroughly, we have also consulted with the provincial and municipal governments and instructed their subordinate military and police to assist the customs in handling the matter. If smuggling of silver or silver coins is found, or those who instigate smuggling, they should immediately report secretly to the nearby customs. If there is no customs location, they can also report to the local financial ministry's affiliated agency or other government agencies for preliminary detention and submit it to the ministry for verification and handling. In order to eliminate private export, the Ministry has specifically formulated generous reward measures, which will be implemented immediately. In addition to consulting separately, it is requested that you review and approve the matter and instruct military and police agencies to comply.

Implementation of Reward and Punishment Law: The reward and punishment measures are stipulated as follows: (1) Seizing smuggled silver coins or silver: In addition to confiscating the silver coins or silver, a penalty of double the amount of smuggling will be imposed, and those who instigate will be severely punished. (2) The silver coins or silver confiscated in the preceding paragraph (after being sold at a price) will be used to award bonuses according to the following method: (A) If the customs or military and police agencies seize them independently, the reward will be doubled according to the customs' method of rewarding informants. That is, for exceptional merit, 60% will be given, and for ordinary merit, 40% will be given. (For example, if 10,000 yuan of smuggled silver coins are seized and confiscated, military police or customs officers with exceptional merit will be awarded 6,000 yuan, and those with ordinary merit will be awarded 4,000 yuan.) (B) If the customs receive a tip from an informant and seize it with the assistance of military and police, the reward will be doubled according to the customs' method of rewarding informants. Military police and informants will each receive 40%, and customs officers will receive 20%. (As in the previous example, military police informants will each receive 4,000 yuan, and customs officers will receive 2,000 yuan.) (C) If the customs seize it based on a tip from an informant (without the assistance of military police), the informant will receive 60% of the reward, and the customs officers will receive 40%. (D) If the customs seize it with the assistance of military police (without a tip from an informant), the military police will receive 40% of the reward, and the customs officers will receive 40%. The names of the informants shall be kept confidential. (3) The double penalty stipulated in item 1 (except for smugglers who escape) cannot be imposed, or the smuggler is unable to pay the fine, the military police informants and customs officers related in items A, B, C, and D of item 2 shall be given 20%, and the remainder shall be turned over to the public.

National Silk Dress Movement

Men's Blue Robe and Black Mandarin Jacket, Women's Blue Dress and Black Skirt

Hope to Comply with National New Year and Various Celebrations

Silk Industry Guild Submission: The city's Silk Industry Guild believes that the National New Year is approaching in an instant, and all circles have celebrations as usual. They should wear national silk dresses to set an example, so they submitted submissions to party and government agencies, requesting that they issue a general order to all levels of the country to comply with the following text: China National Party Executive Committee, Executive Yuan, Ministry of Interior, Shanghai Municipal Party Department, Shanghai Municipal Government, I sincerely believe that promoting national goods is an urgent task for the present, and rescuing silk is an especially urgent and important task. The national silk is gorgeous and rich, and it once shone all over the world. Clothing is a tool for showing one's body, and the civilization of the country is what one sees. Since the revolution, short foreign clothes have become popular in temples. Clothes are not neat, and the people lose their image. Profits overflow, and the national economy is declining. I think about the future and feel cold. I submitted to the Ministry of Interior on April 16, 1929, and promulgated the clothing regulations, which limited the use of domestic goods. At that time, I thought that the government and education would change the fashion. After several years, the laws and regulations are the same as the shackles. The use of foreign countries to change China is now fierce. The sales of national silk have decreased day by day, and the import of foreign goods has increased with time. The blood of the national economic lifeline is on the verge of exhaustion. The psychology of Chinese people loving foreign goods is booming. Thinking of this, I feel trembling. I think again and again that the way to save is only two ways. On the one hand, the silk manufacturing industry should improve its products to meet the needs of the society. On the other hand, I look forward to the enthusiastic promotion of party and government personnel and their personal practice, so as to achieve the effect of the wind. Silk is originally a fine and special product of our country, with a long and glorious history. In recent years, manufacturers have carefully studied, purchased machines, and strived for improvement. Silk products are enough to be beautiful in Europe and the West. In addition, the price of silk has fallen, and the price of national silk is low. It is almost the same as imported cloth. All of these have facts to follow. They are not just empty words. It is only because the Chinese people are obsessed with Europeanization, short foreign clothes, and boast to each other. They take materials from imported woolen cloth, and do not hesitate to spend money like dirt. They despise domestic silk, and do not care about the cheap price. The dynasty and the field follow the custom, and the whole country is crazy. Last year, silk merchants lost their profits, and silk factories went bankrupt one after another. How many people lost their jobs? This year, western Zhejiang is drought-stricken, and silkworms have no market for sale. The displaced people are related, and the hungry people are everywhere. If we do not try to save it now, how can we imagine the future? I think it is related to the national economy and the people's livelihood, not just the silk industry. For this reason, I urgently appeal to your council, court, and government to issue a general order to all public officials and personnel to set an example and be a guide for the people. They should strictly comply with the clothing regulations. Men's formal attire should be a blue robe and a black mandarin jacket, and women's formal attire should be a blue dress and a black skirt. The materials should all be limited to domestic goods. From now on, ceremonies and important meetings, as well as happy events, funerals, etc., should be dressed in national silk dresses to set an example. The National New Year is approaching in an instant, and all circles have celebrations as usual. I especially hope to take this opportunity to issue a general order to comply with it, so that the top will follow the bottom, the decline will be saved, and the men will follow the women, and the national silk is expected to turn around. The hair is tied in one stroke, and it is here. In addition to sending separate telegrams, I respectfully request your council, court, and government to review and approve and quickly issue a general order to comply with it. The national economy and the people's livelihood are really dependent on it. Luo Qinghua, chairman of the Shanghai Silk Industry Guild, kowtows respectfully.

Haili's Maiden Voyage Today

Sailors and Shipowners Are Considering

The position of captain was initially intended to be filled by Puan's Laux. He also sank a sailboat outside the port of Qingdao, which has not been resolved. And the ship does not carry passengers to Hong Kong, so there is no need to send a foreign captain. Therefore, the bureau has not yet filled out the commission, and the general shipowner and the head of the shipping department are still discussing it carefully. Because the bureau has many experienced Chinese shipowners, it is still under consideration. The carpets in the first-class cabins of the four new ships have been made of excellent quality, but the carpets are woven with the national emblem. The bureau believes that the national emblem should be given special respect. Weaving it on the carpets and stepping on it is not appropriate. Therefore, it has ordered the captains of the four ships to remove the original national emblem carpets and store them in the bureau, and purchase new carpets of superior quality to replace them. The shipping department is still studying and improving the equipment of the four ships. The life jackets for passengers are planned to be the latest and most efficient. Request from the Taxpayers' Association to the Municipal Council to Refrain from Overestimating Rent

Market Slump Leads to Lower Rent

Addressing Financial Shortfalls Should Start with Vacant Properties

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Respectfully, according to a letter from Chen Yueshan, Chen Yueshan resides at No. 71, Lane 112, Sanguantang Lane, Public Concession. This house was built by the China Business Company in 1923 and rented for 40 yuan per month. In 1927, I purchased it, continuing to pay taxes based on the 40 yuan rent. This has been the case for over ten years without any issues. In February of this year, I also built a house on the vacant land next door, which was completed in May. In December and January, it was rented to Chongdao Hall for 40 yuan per month. Unexpectedly, the foreign tax collector of the Municipal Council wanted to calculate the tax based on a monthly rent of 60 yuan. Despite explaining this several times and providing the lease as proof, they refused to accept it. Reluctantly, I went to the tax office of the Municipal Council several times to explain, but to no avail. Furthermore, they escalated the situation, attempting to increase the rent assessment of my residence at No. 71, where I have lived for over ten years, to 80 yuan. They even threatened to increase it to 100 yuan if I did not comply. The Municipal Council's tax collection is based on the level of rent. My residence at No. 71 and the newly built No. 69 next door share a total area of about five fen. Based on a land value of 20,000 yuan per mu, the land value is 10,000 yuan, and the construction cost of both houses is 7,000 yuan, totaling 17,000 yuan. The monthly rent for both houses is 80 yuan, with a monthly interest rate of about five percent. In the current market, a five percent interest rate is not low. If the foreign tax collector wants to overestimate the rent, they are welcome to rent it from the Municipal Council. Moreover, when I first moved here, the area was quite desolate. To this day, streetlights have not been installed, the public pit opposite has not been removed, and the main road to the east is filled with collapsed carts. The situation has not improved in decades. Furthermore, the residents nearby are mostly dockworkers, living in very unsanitary conditions. Every summer, they sleep outside in the ditches. They are ignorant of public morality, and the police do not intervene. Daily access is difficult. I only remain here because the house is my own property, and moving elsewhere is not economically feasible. In the current economic downturn, it is common to see tenants demanding rent reductions, and landlords voluntarily reducing rents. For example, the rent for Hartung's properties on Nanjing Road is so high that they remain vacant and generate no income. If the rent for my house is overestimated and taxes are increased, no one will want to rent it. The tax collector ignores the market situation and rashly increases taxes by more than half, which is unreasonable. I have been fulfilling my tax obligations in the concession for over ten years. Now, the tax collector only knows how to increase taxes, while neglecting public health and road traffic. After much consideration, I cannot remain silent. I have long admired your association as the leader of Chinese residents in the concession, so I dare to present this matter directly, requesting that you forward a letter to the Municipal Council's tax office, urging them to consider the market situation when dealing with residents in the concession and to refrain from arbitrarily imposing taxes." Upon arrival, the Shanghai market was found to be even more desolate. Silver exports are shrinking, and the daily dismantling rate is as high as four corners, with chips being even more scarce. This is a matter of deep concern for those who care about the market. If the municipal authorities do not reduce or even maintain the existing tax rates, it is uncertain whether the situation will improve. If, on the one hand, the value of real estate is declining, and on the other hand, they maintain high rents or overestimate land values or rents to increase taxes, then under the dual pressure, the liquidation of shops and the relocation of residences will be an inevitable result of the contraction of the social economy. Taxpayers foresee this phenomenon, taking Nanjing Road as an example, and have already seen its beginnings. How they themselves struggle to overcome the difficulties is a matter that can be temporarily set aside. It is deeply known that the bureau's resulting shortfall in tax revenue is a fact that is difficult to avoid, so the delegation authorized the bureau to implement a case of levying a general tax on vacant houses that passed the recent representative conference, it has been delayed and no facts have been seen, and instead, one began by estimating higher rent, which was only limited to hotels, etc. in the central district, and recently also to undeveloped areas that have been disturbed, we must know that the small number of stores that recently opened on Nanjing Road have an understanding with the landlord, and are of a completely trial nature, and the rent is not counted at all, if one only knows its surface but does not know its actual content, increase the general tax bit by bit, then the public increase is not much, the private sector has already been exhausted, and as a result, the tax loss due to vacant houses without tax will be higher than the income from the increased tax, because the individual relationship is very great, therefore a particularly earnest letter is sent to your bureau, urging the tax office to plan as a whole, so that seeking benefit causes damage to be important, this is addressed to the head office of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council.

Qingpu Steamer Runs Aground on Black Sandbar

The Yangtze River is shallow, especially in the area of Black Sandbar in Wuhu (near Hama-ga-Iso, where Sanbei Company's Matsuura ran aground). The water depth there is only seven or eight feet, making it difficult for heavily laden vessels to pass. The Wuhu Customs has issued measures for lightering and maintaining the waterway. Unexpectedly, the Sanbei Company's Matsuura steamer had just been towed out of the shallows when the Qingpu steamer, which was sailing upstream from Shanghai on the 23rd, ran aground in the same area due to the shallow water. It is reported that the Qingpu's draft is over eleven feet, which is significantly different from the water depth in the area. Therefore, although other Yangtze River vessels were ordered to tow it, it was difficult to achieve any effect. It is now planned to lighter the Qingpu steamer's cargo before attempting to tow it. Other Yangtze River steamers are also preparing to lighter cargo at that location to avoid being stranded.

Pan Yangyao Discusses the Business Conditions of Various Industries Over the Past Year

Money Shops Invest More in Rural Areas

National Products Industry Also Developing Daily

In order to understand the business conditions of various industries in Shanghai over the past year, a reporter from the Central News Agency specially visited Mr. Pan Yangyao, who is familiar with the situation of various industries in Shanghai, yesterday and inquired about the situation of various industries. According to Mr. Pan, the money shop industry and the national products industry have made significant progress this year. The details are as follows:

Money Shop Industry: According to Mr. Pan, the business conditions of the money shop industry over the past year, with the exception of firms with shorter capital, had surpluses. Although several small banks in the city went bankrupt this year, this does not mean the decline of Shanghai's money shop industry. The banks with shorter capital have inflexible turnover, and most of their operations are speculative, and their internal organizations lack integrity, and therefore went bankrupt, it is not related to the money shop industry itself. This year, the banking authorities, in view of the danger of the concentration of silver in the city, have been engaged in rural lending. Statistics show that the city's banks invested more than 10 million in rural lending. Although the interest on this loan is thin and the formalities are cumbersome, rural borrowers value credit and are able to recover the funds on schedule, so banks believe that investing in rural lending is a sound and solid business and are happy to operate. The major banks are currently engaged in rural surveys in various places in order to increase the amount of investment in the coming year. According to the Bank Savings Law promulgated by the Ministry of Finance, the number of rural loans invested should account for one-fifth of the savings, while the total amount invested by banks this year is only 10 million yuan, which is very different from the provisions of the Bank Savings Law, so it was decided to actively invest in rural loans in various places from next year. As for rural finance in various places, with the exception of those who are in arrears due to disasters, the rest have had bumper harvests, and Shaanxi's cotton harvest reached 50 million yuan, and Xuchang's tobacco harvest reached more than 40 million yuan, which is unprecedented in previous years. Rural finance is ample, and next year's loans will inevitably increase as a result, which can be asserted. It is a good phenomenon that banks directly and indirectly actively invest in the interior, he said.

Cotton Mill Industry: As for the cotton mill industry, although there was no progress in the business conditions this year, the cotton mill authorities, in view of the industry's lifelessness, are actively seeking to improve methods. Rong Zongjing went to the Northwest for inspection and has now begun to organize the Cotton Yarn Industry Improvement Association to discuss improvement methods. The reasons for the decline of the cotton mill industry are: one is due to the shortage of capital and the heavy interest on the loan, the interest on the loan by the cotton mill is always between one point and nine points, and the interest on the loan by the Japanese cotton mill is only about two or three points, and the difference between the two is huge. As for the cost of each package of 20-count yarn, China needs more than 26 yuan, while Japanese yarn only needs about 18 yuan. The management of cotton mills is not as good as that of Japanese factories. For example, in China's cotton mills, 400 workers are required to manage every 10,000 spindles. Even if the system is improved now, 300 workers are still required. Japanese factories only need 180 workers. For these reasons, they cannot compete with Japanese yarn, and the business is declining daily. Several cotton mills had surpluses this year. The factory authorities are now working hard to improve, so there is hope starting next year. The flour industry had surpluses in the first half of the year and was normal in the second half of the year.

National Products Industry: The national products industry was in the best condition this year, with the machinery and electrical appliance industries being the best. The development of these two industries is a natural trend, and it is expected that they will develop more and more in the future. Because the interior is happy to purchase, such as electric lights, electric fans, agricultural tools, etc., have been purchased in large quantities, so the two industries have a large surplus. Although the reasons for their development are due to this, the increase in the import tax on large goods machinery and the reduction of the import tax on machinery raw materials are also small reasons. The silk and satin industry's business this year, although better than last year, but the profits are getting thinner year by year. The enamel industry is also developing, but the selling price is always below cost, and solutions are being discussed to maintain it. As for the dyeing and weaving industry, the dyeing industry has a surplus, while the weaving industry is not prosperous. As for small industries such as hot water bottle industry, bakelite industry, etc., they are all manufacturing abuse, and factory closures are piled on, which is a pity. The rubber industry is also in the end of its rope due to excessive competition among its peers, and the industrial community should pay attention to it, he said.

Ministry Order Disallows Bail in Counterfeit Money Case

Released and Then Detained Again

Guard Accused of Fraud by Family

Liu Shouquan, a native of Qingjiang, residing at No. 296, Calle Road, French Concession, is 42 years old and a barber. In October of last year, he was arrested by the French Concession police for counterfeiting money. After interrogation by the Second Special Court, he was sentenced to one year and six months in prison and fined 50 yuan. After the sentence was confirmed, he was sent to the Second Special District Prison to serve his sentence. In October of this year, one year had passed. Liu entrusted someone to submit a petition requesting the prison to release him on bail in accordance with the law. After the prison approved the request, Liu was released on bail on October 26 and sent home. The prison reported the matter to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, which then forwarded it to the Ministry of Justice. The Ministry issued an order stating that Liu's crime did not meet the bail conditions and rejected the request, ordering that he continue to serve his sentence. When the ministry order arrived at the prison, Liu had already been released on bail for more than a month. On the 14th of this month, the prison sent a guard, Zhang He, to summon Liu and ordered him to continue serving his sentence. Liu's wife, Liu Wangshi, believed that her husband had already been released on bail and was suddenly summoned to serve his sentence. She recalled that during the summer of this year, a prison guard from Yangzhou named Wang Jiahan had come to her home on behalf of her husband to collect money, saying that he could guarantee a successful bail motion and had borrowed three yuan. Now that her husband had suddenly been summoned to serve his sentence, she believed that Wang had been to her home before and knew her address, so Wang Jiahen was definitely behind the matter. She went to the Second Special Prison to report that the guard had committed fraud and requested an investigation. After the warden summoned the guard Wang Jiakun for questioning, he prepared a document and transferred it to the Second Special Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation and interrogation. Yesterday, Prosecutor Wang Ren and clerk Peng Yu interrogated him in the fifth court. First, they heard the plaintiff Liu Wangshi's account of Jia Kun's fraud. When asked, Wang confessed that the first time he took three yuan from Liu Wangshi, it was Liu Shouquan who asked me to take it to buy a undershirt and health shirt. The second time he took three yuan was because my mother died and I joined Liu Wangshi for a share to reach 30 yuan to buy a coffin. In addition, he never took a penny, etc. The official also summoned the witnesses Liu Jinrong, guard Zhang He, and prisoner Liu Shouquan for questioning. They ordered a new verification to be heard later. After Liu Shouquan was released on bail, he was rejected by order of the ministry, and after the case was summoned to continue execution, the prosecutor of the High Third Branch had also opened and brought Liu to the case to investigate the circumstances of his request for bail.

Fireworks Industry Association Appeals for Exemption from Prohibition

Fireworks are a Sanitary Product

Greatly Affecting People's Livelihoods

Since the news of the joint consultation between the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus on banning fireworks was published in various newspapers on the 22nd of this month, the business of various fireworks shops has been greatly affected. Fireworks workers are uneasy. The Fireworks Industry Association has appealed to party and government agencies separately to exempt them from the ban. Its petition to the Social Affairs Bureau reads: "It is submitted for the purpose of earnestly requesting exemption from the prohibition, so as to maintain livelihoods and save commerce. I read in the newspapers of December 12 and 22 that your bureau sent personnel to consult with the Public Security Bureau on the prohibition of fireworks, which was shocking and inexplicable. I believe that the firecrackers a kind of unique handicraft product that has been around for thousands of years in our country, its function is to eliminate mountain mist and sea miasma, change bad air, refresh people's spirits, and help people's interests, so it is not only loved by the people of the whole country, but also welcomed by all countries in the world, occupying an important position in export goods, and the customs has records to check. The sales volume is the largest in Southeast Asia, because the miasma is the heaviest there, even in today's scientific age, if not for the gas of firecrackers and sulfur, there is no way to eliminate it, this is also iron evidence that firecrackers will not be affected by scientific invention and will be eliminated. There are those who do not have a deep understanding of the function of firecrackers, and presumptuously think that they are useless waste, but they do not know that the Hankou Fireworks Industry Association has submitted it to the Central Ministry of Health for chemical verification and determined that it is a sanitary product, and the original case is in place. This is only regarding the function of firecrackers, as for the statistics of workers and merchants engaged in the fireworks industry in the country, there are no less than millions. At this time when commercial depression, rural collapse, and economic depression are seriously enveloping, the fireworks industry is already dying, if the government authorities do not vigorously protect this nationwide handicraft industry, but inflict harm on it, then the future of people's livelihoods is truly unthinkable. Try to just prohibit the lighting of fireworks, the solution. If citizens do not light them, then the goods have no way out, the capital of firecrackers merchants will be turned into nothing, and the livelihood of firecrackers workers will be on the verge of extinction, in a flash, putting millions of firecrackers workers and merchants in the whole country in a place where they cannot live or die, why is the heart of your bureau so cruel? Even if it is to prohibit useless consumption, among the imported goods, there are thousands of types, and it is possible to shift the target and do so, sages think it is impossible to hate what the people like, I hope that your bureau will show mercy and exempt from prohibition, trembling and crying, I hope that you will show your compassion."

Verdict Reached in Yi Fangshuo Case

Sentencing Scheduled for the 27th

Yi's Request for Bail Denied

Yi Fangshuo, a 43-year-old from Hangzhou residing at No. 147, Baxianfang Alley, Huage Nie Road in the French Concession, who performs comic acts and songs without theatrical scripts at the rooftop amusement park of the New New Company, forcibly raped his 19-year-old cousin Yi Baozhu and kept her under constant surveillance, forbidding her to step out of line. On the morning of the 11th of this month, at 10:00 AM, Baozhu finally managed to escape and reported to the French police station. The vice squad dispatched detectives to arrest Yi, along with his concubines Yi Caitao and Yi Meimei, his younger brother, and fourteen young female actors from his troupe. Investigation revealed that in addition to raping his cousin Baozhu, he had also raped his 13-year-old cousin Li Xiaozhen twice, and sold women named Ye Jinzhu and Yang Lingzhu, making them

learn to perform opera, etc. The police station, based on Articles 240, 243, 257, and 316 of the criminal code, regarding offenses against public morals, family, and freedom, filed a public prosecution with the Special No. 2 Court. Judge Zhang Chaozuo held two hearings. Yi Baozhu and Li Xiaozhu suddenly requested to withdraw their accusations regarding the rape incidents. Subsequently, because the victims Ye Jinzhu and Yang Lingzhu did not appear in court for the cases of obstructing family and freedom under Articles 257 and 316, the trial could not proceed. The court adjourned the hearing to a later date, and Yi Baozhu and Li Xiaozhen were allowed to be taken back by their guardians, Yi Hu and Ben Duo Fu, respectively, as previously reported. Yesterday, the hearing was resumed. Judge Zhang specially opened the Second Criminal Court for the trial. Lawyer Fei Xizhen represented the police station. The court ordered Yi to be brought in and first instructed Detective Bao, who was in charge of the case, to report on the

case investigation. According to the defending lawyers, the mothers of Ye Jinzhu and Yang Lingzhu had arrived in court today and requested to be questioned. The court asked the defendant Yi Fangshuo about the background of the two girls. Yi Fangshuo replied, "Yang Lingzhu is 13 years old this year. She was sent by my sister last year around March or April to learn opera. She was brought by my sister from the countryside as an adopted daughter-in-law, to be married to my nephew. There are seven or eight girls in my household, five are students, and the rest are my own people. The terms of learning opera were all agreed upon verbally, without any contract. During the learning period, they eat at my expense, and after they learn, I recommend them or have them

perform in my troupe. Ye Jinzhu is the daughter of Section Chief Ye, sent to me to learn opera. She is very lively, and has fallen and injured herself severely twice. She was sent to the hospital to be treated, so she needs to be accompanied when she goes out, which does not infringe on their freedom. I teach them by giving advice, and do not beat them. I did not buy the two girls with money," etc. At this point, the court ordered Yi to be taken down and summoned Ye Jinzhu to the stand. The girl testified, "I am 14 years old, born in the Year of the Rooster, and from Hangzhou. I live at No. 28, Fachangli in Hangzhou. My father is Ye Qiuda, formerly a trainee in the Water Police Bureau. I have never been beaten. When I am not performing opera, I play at home and am very free. I am accompanied when I go out. I did not say at the police station that I was sold to Yi for 150 yuan."

Summon Yang Lingzhu. She testified, "I am 12 years old, born in the Year of the Pig, and from Hangzhou. I live at No. 2, Xinchang Road in Hangzhou. I have parents, and my father's name is Yang Debing. Last year in June, my mother sent me to my uncle Yi Fangshuo's house to play. I wanted to learn opera myself. I have not been beaten by Yi." At this point, the court summoned Ye Jinzhu's mother, Ye Li, to the stand. She stated, "Jinzhu was born to my older sister. Because I have no children, she was given to me. I took her in for breastfeeding a few months after she was born. Now my older sister lives in Taiping Lane in Nanjing. My husband, Ye Qiuda, was a section chief during Xu's tenure in the Water Police Bureau. He was previously a soldier on a warship and is away from home. Because I have no son, I sent Jinzhu to Yi's place to learn opera, hoping to rely on her in the future. There is no way I would have sold her to Yi Fangshuo for a price. Please investigate." Furthermore, according to Yang Yi (Yi Fangshuo's sister), "My husband currently works on the Yuhe warship. Lingzhu is from Changbang Village in the countryside. Her father is dead, and her mother has remarried. My mother brought the child to me when she was six years old to be my daughter-in-law. My son is now 11 years old," etc. The court also summoned the original plaintiff, Yi Baozhu, to the stand. The court asked, "Did he beat you while you were learning opera in the defendant's house? Did he monitor your actions?" Yi replied, "I came to Shanghai last November to learn opera, but I couldn't learn it. I wasn't beaten, but he often scolded me. Sometimes when I went out, he would insist that I go with him, otherwise he would scold me, saying that I was going to find a lover," etc. Li Xiaozhen also testified that she came to Shanghai in July of this year to learn to dance. She had not been beaten or monitored. At this point, the court considered the evidence to be complete and ordered the defendant to be brought in, then declared

the beginning of the debate. After the police station's lawyer and the defendant's lawyers debated with each other, the court announced the end of the debate and scheduled sentencing for 9:00 AM on the 27th. The defendant was remanded into custody. After the defendant's lawyer repeatedly requested that the defendant be allowed bail, the court refused, stating that the case was proceeding quickly and there were only a few days until sentencing. The defendant then requested to be transferred to the detention center, which the court approved and issued a warrant. The bailiffs took the defendant down and sent him to the detention center. The case has attracted the attention of the entire city of Shanghai. At each hearing, the seats were filled with spectators. Because listening was prohibited, onlookers could not hear the trial. Yesterday's trial had nearly 200 onlookers. Because the case concerned offenses against family and freedom, the court did not prohibit onlookers, causing the Second Court to be very crowded, with barely any room to stand. The court had to disperse the crowd.

Manager of Jiande Bank Branch Accuses General Manager of Embezzlement

A Title Deed Used as Security

Never Returned After Resignation

Jiande Bank, located at No. 16, North Henan Road in this city, recently announced its closure due to poor business and financial difficulties, and hired lawyers and accountants to register and liquidate the company. Recently, Jin Jialu, a local resident (36 years old, residing at No. 881, East Youheng Road), the manager of the Jiande Bank branch in Zhonghongqiao, hired lawyers Zhan Jifeng and Zhan Yigang to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Division of the First Special Court, accusing Jiande Bank and its General Manager Chai Changgui of embezzling a deposited title deed. The lawsuit requested a judgment according to the law, along with a private prosecution. The main points of the lawsuit stated that the plaintiff was introduced by a friend and hired by Chai Changgui, the General Manager of Jiande Bank headquarters in Shanghai, to serve as the manager of the Zhonghongqiao branch. He initially declined, but was persuaded to try it for a few days. According to custom, a security deposit was required to guarantee the plaintiff's financial responsibilities during his tenure. The plaintiff then deposited title deed No. 13829, registered in England, with the defendant and received a deposit receipt. At that time, the plaintiff stated to the defendant that this title deed was not solely owned by the plaintiff, and that the condition of the deposit was only to guarantee the plaintiff's responsibilities. On November 26th of this year, after the plaintiff went to the branch to oversee matters and audit the accounts, he discovered errors in the accounts and discrepancies in the inventory. He realized that the defendant's hiring of the plaintiff had ulterior motives, so he wrote a letter of resignation on the 3rd of this month to avoid being held responsible for others' mistakes. The defendant replied with a letter of approval, but requested that the title deed, which was deposited as security, be returned within two months. After receiving the letter, the plaintiff was deeply surprised, as the deposit receipt clearly stated that this security item should be returned at the time of resignation. Upon further investigation, it was discovered that the title deed had been used by the defendant as collateral. Under these circumstances, the defendant's hiring of the plaintiff as branch manager clearly had illegal intentions. Now, the defendant has privately mortgaged the deposited property, which violates Article 357 of the criminal code. Therefore, the plaintiff filed a lawsuit requesting that the defendant be summoned to court and punished according to the law, and also filed a civil suit, requesting that the defendant immediately return the title deed deposited by the plaintiff, as well as all damages, etc. Yesterday at around 1:00 PM, Judge Wu Zehan presided over the Third Criminal Court for questioning. The defendant Chai Changgui also surrendered to the court with his lawyer, Cai Liucheng. The plaintiff, Jin Jialu, surrendered to the court and testified to the above circumstances. When questioned, the defendant admitted to mortgaging the title deed, but claimed that he had obtained the plaintiff's consent and that it had been stamped at the time. Judge Wu reviewed the testimony and stated that further investigation was necessary. He adjourned the hearing to 3:30 PM on the 28th at the Second Court. The plaintiff's lawyer, Zhan Jifeng, stated that the defendant was at risk of fleeing and that the amount involved was quite large, totaling more than 20,000 yuan. He requested that the defendant be ordered to post bail. The court ordered Chai to provide a guarantor to be available upon summons and to await questioning outside.

Fine of Two Hundred Yuan

Police Announce Appeal

Chen Wu, a Guangdong woman residing at No. 723, Tiantong Road, was arrested this month for abusing her 12-year-old adopted daughter, Xu Xing, with wooden sticks, rattan canes, small iron hammers, branding irons, and other instruments, causing severe injuries. Detectives were dispatched to escort Chen, along with the evidence, to the First Special District Court for detailed questioning, as reported in this newspaper. The girl was temporarily placed in the Jiliang Institute. The court ordered Chen to be remanded in custody to await sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan presided over the Third Criminal Court and sentenced Chen Wu to a fine of 200 yuan, confiscated the evidence, and ordered that Xu be kept in the Jiliang Institute. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, announced an appeal, which the court granted.

Ministry of Finance Postpones Ban on Cigarette Coupons

Ban Effective March 1, 1935

The Ministry of Finance's order to ban cigarette coupons has been repeatedly petitioned by the Chinese Cigarette Factory Association to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance, requesting a reversal of the decision in order to maintain the struggling businesses. The Ministry of Finance has now issued a notice to all factories in all provinces and cities, temporarily allowing the inclusion of coupons in cigarette packs until the end of February 1935. From March onwards, all cigarettes leaving the factory must not include coupons. Those that have already left the factory and been shipped to various places for sale will still be allowed to be sold as usual.

Revised Price for Multiple Copies of Social Telegrams

Only Ten Cents for Every Fifty Characters

The prices of domestic social telegrams are low, and all sectors have long been happy to send them. Recently, the Ministry of Communications stipulated that, effective December 25th of this month, the fee for multiple copies of social telegrams (i.e., the fee for sending several copies in the same location) will be changed to ten cents in silver dollars for every fifty characters (previously calculated as two cents in silver dollars for every fifty characters, the same as ordinary telegrams). Less than fifty characters will also be counted as fifty characters, and the price will increase accordingly. The Shanghai Telegraph Bureau in this city notified yesterday that it will be implemented as scheduled. In addition, the social telegrams with celebratory themes this year have been very popular due to the attractive paper, so business is very crowded.

New Songjiang Society's Perch

The four-gilled perch is a specialty of Rongcheng, with red gills and jade-like body, resembling the fish in the pond. Perch sashimi and perch soup have long been known to people outside the city, but because there is not much production, many places use other fish to make up the numbers. Now that the winter solstice is approaching, it is the time when perch are on the market. The New Songjiang Society in Songjiang has specially opened a dining hall in the newly built Great Summer Building, and hired famous local chefs to prepare exquisite dishes to meet the demands of people from all over. The local scenery is well-prepared, and the flavor is naturally different. If people from other places want to taste the authentic and unique flavor, why not take a trip and try it? The New Songjiang Society is located dozens of steps east of Songjiang Station, making it very convenient to travel to and from.

Rickshaw Merchants Request Exemption from Removing Mezzanines

Petition Submitted to Dongjiadu Police Station Yesterday

Chief Yi Has Agreed to Stop the Removal

Rickshaw merchants in the Qinglong Bridge area of Nanmatou, because the Dongjiadu Police Station has recently ordered the demolition of the mezzanines built by various rickshaw shops, believing that they are prone to danger, and has notified each household through the police, have been in a state of anxiety and cannot live in peace. They have requested the Shanghai Rickshaw Trade Association to submit a report to the city chamber of commerce and request the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to stop the demolition. Yesterday (the 24th) at 8:00 AM, they gathered at a certain teahouse to discuss solutions. Fifty or sixty households attended. Hu Wenqing, Zhu Yutian, and Wang Rongqing were elected as representatives to petition the police station. Chief Yi Zuanren personally received them. The representatives stated that the mezzanines in the rickshaw shops were built because the rent was too expensive and there was no way to accommodate so many rickshaw pullers. The rickshaw pullers come and go from time to time, and if they were to rent houses to live in, it would not only be inconvenient, but also beyond their financial means. Therefore, before the government builds affordable housing for the common people, the demolition of these mezzanines should be stopped in order to ensure the peace of the people and avoid disturbances. Chief Yi considered that the request was based on the facts and ordered the rickshaw merchants to organize themselves to prevent accidents, and agreed to stop the demolition. The representatives were satisfied and withdrew.

Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company Reports Mid-Trip Attack

Were the Perpetrators Impersonating Bandits?

Please Conduct a Thorough Investigation

The incident in which the Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company's last bus from Luodian Town to Shanghai Station was attacked by bandits on the way the day before yesterday evening has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now, we will reproduce the original telegram from the company to the Baoshan County Government: To Baoshan County Government, County Chief Longxun, On the afternoon of December 22nd, at 5:00 PM, the company's last bus, City Photo No. 958, traveling from Luodian to Shanghai, driven by driver Huang Zhaoqi, was suddenly fired upon by two men in gray military uniforms at the intersection of Dachang City River Bridge and Jiangchang Road. The bullet shattered a piece of glass in the front right corner of the bus and grazed the driver's face, causing great danger. Fortunately, there was only one passenger on the bus, surnamed Xu, who was not hit by the stray bullet. Huang Zhaoqi immediately stopped the bus and asked for the reason. They said that they had orders from their superiors to stop the bus for inspection. They then took off Huang's and the passenger's tops and searched them, finding nothing. They waved the bus to proceed and told Huang that there would be inspectors at Dachang Station. Huang reasoned that even if they wanted to search, they should not have fired a shot suddenly. After arguing for a long time, they dispersed after being persuaded by passersby. When the bus arrived at Dachang Station, it found that the police and security team were densely stationed in front of the station, waiting to inspect the passing vehicles. Huang immediately reported the shooting to the station chief. The local Public Security Bureau Chief Zhou and the captain of the security team stationed there were also at the station. After hearing the news, they believed that it must have been bandits and led the team to the scene of the incident on the bus to investigate, but found no trace of bandits and stopped. According to reports from other drivers of the company (i.e., the last buses from Liuhe, Jiading, etc. returning to Shanghai), on the same day, the last buses passing through the Jiangchang Road intersection were stopped and searched by men in gray military uniforms waiting there. A passenger, Xiting, the vice president of the Liuhe Huizhong Hospital, can testify, because he was also on the last bus and witnessed the search. The search took place at dusk, and the area was not remote. It is strange and serious that bandits dared to impersonate security team soldiers and police, and at the same time conducted the same search on passing vehicles at the same location less than half a mile away. We have specially inspected and photographed the bullet-damaged glass window of passenger car No. 958 and telegraphed the facts truthfully. We hope that you will quickly investigate and ensure transportation and the safety of travelers. The Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company's Manager Zhu Zengyuan and Deputy Manager Hong Bao Ying respectfully request, December 23rd, 1934.

Bao Jiuru Abducts a Relative's Daughter

Lan Ying, the four-year-old daughter of Lu Shi, a woman from Tongzhou residing at No. 605 Huarong Road, disappeared while playing in front of her door at 3:35 PM on the 14th of this month. After a frantic search proved fruitless, she urgently reported the incident to the Yulin Road police station. Detective Li Pengfei and officer Wu Shoushan were dispatched to investigate. On the previous day, the suspects, Bao Jiuru from Tongzhou and Miao Yulin from Changzhou, were apprehended on Yangzhou Road. Miao claimed that the child was at the home of Wang Fuyuan, a Changzhou native, at No. 20 Wengjiatang, Zhabei. The officers then went to the location with detectives from the relevant Public Security Bureau and arrested Wang. Wang confessed that Zhang A'si, a Jiangbei native who ran a matchmaking shop, had arranged the sale to Huo Su, a Guangdong woman residing at No. 47 Dengtuo Road, for 28 yuan. Zhang was subsequently apprehended on Huade Road. Upon questioning Huo Su at her residence, it was revealed that Lu's daughter had been sent to Liang Su, a fellow villager, at No. 320 Public Security Lane, Wusong Road. The child was retrieved, and Huo Su and four other men and women were taken into custody and detained separately. The child was returned to her mother, Lu Shi. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Li Zhishan from the Municipal Council presented the preliminary facts, followed by a report from the Chinese and Western detectives detailing the investigation. The plaintiff, Lu Shi, stated that the defendant, Bao Jiuru, was a relative and had lured Lan Ying away and conspired with Miao, Wang, and Zhang to sell her to Huo Su and others. When questioned, Bao Jiuru confessed that Wang Fuyuan had given Miao 27 yuan after the fact, which was then given to him. Miao Yulin confessed that he was the one who brought Lu's daughter and entrusted Wang Fuyuan to sell her, receiving only three yuan. Wang Fuyuan confessed that Bao brought the girl on the 17th, claiming she was his daughter, and gave evasive answers to other questions. Zhang A'si confessed to receiving only one yuan. Huo Su confessed that her husband had passed away, leaving her with a son, and that she had paid 59 yuan to legally adopt the girl as a daughter-in-law. Both Miao and Wang were present at the time. Wang claimed she was his own daughter, and that he was selling her due to poverty, and signed the agreement. She was unaware she was buying an abducted child and begged for leniency. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered Huo Su to post bail of 300 yuan and remanded the others in custody for further investigation at a later date.

Municipal Government Orders Dredging of the Huangzihulu River

The farmland in the Yangsi Tangqiao area of this city is contiguous. Due to the impact of this year's drought, the autumn harvest has been poor. In addition to petitioning the authorities for a reduction or exemption of land taxes, the Huangzihulu River in the area has not been dredged for many years, which has greatly affected agricultural production. A petition was submitted to the Municipal Government to allocate funds for dredging. The Municipal Government has now ordered the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to take advantage of the current winter slack season to recruit laborers to dredge the river. It is reported that the Municipal Bureau of Public Works has decided to first send personnel to inspect the site and then immediately begin recruiting laborers to start dredging, hoping to complete the project during this period to benefit agricultural production.

Second-Class Sleeping Car Tickets for the Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai) Railway

Attached to Night Express Trains Nos. 5 and 6

Upper and Lower Berth Prices to be Implemented

The Jinghu Railway has added second-class sleeping cars. The Wusong Locomotive Factory is using existing first-class car chassis to initially assemble two cars, numbered 623 and 624. The work has been completed, and they are scheduled to start service on New Year's Day of the 24th year [of the Republic]. The up train will be attached to the No. 6 Shanghai-Beijing Night Express, and the down train will be attached to the No. 5 Beijing-Shanghai Night Express. Each car has 60 seats for daytime travel and 30 berths for nighttime travel. The interior equipment is identical to that of the second-class sleeping cars currently operating on the Shanghai-Ping (Beijing) through train. The sleeping berth fee is set at 2.50 yuan per passenger for the upper berth and 3 yuan for the lower berth.

Pig Trade Mediation Resolves "Exit Fee" Dispute, Slaughtering Not Halted

Seeking Fundamental Solution for Slaughtering Operations

Petitions to Party and Government Organs and Declaration Issued

Nine pig stalls in this port city, including Huang Shunxing, Wu Yixing, Wanlong, Jiuda, Xingji, Chen Yuexing, Sanxing, Xinglin, and Changshun, collect an "exit fee" of two cents per pig from slaughtering businesses, which has provoked strong opposition from the slaughtering industry. Yesterday was the scheduled start date for the fee collection. All slaughtering businesses in the city unanimously stopped picking up pigs, creating a very serious situation. Later, the pig trade took steps to stop the collection and asked the slaughtering businesses to pick up pigs as usual, averting a halting of slaughtering. The slaughtering businesses sent representatives to petition the Nanjing Municipal Government and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The details are as follows:

Normal Pig Pickup Resumed: The nine pig stalls in the Nanshi area issued a notice the day before yesterday, stating that ticket sales would begin yesterday and an "exit fee" of two cents per pig would be collected from slaughtering businesses. The slaughtering businesses held a meeting the day before yesterday, resolving that if the fee was collected, they would unanimously stop picking up pigs. After 10:00 AM yesterday, in front of the pig stalls at Xuejia浜, Youche Wharf, Nanshi, the pig stalls hired a large number of non-industry idlers, attempting to force the slaughtering businesses to buy tickets and grab pigs. Seeing this situation, the slaughtering businesses immediately stopped picking up pigs to avoid conflicts. The two sides were at a stalemate, and the situation was very serious. Upon hearing the news, the pig trade believed that the pig stalls' actions would hinder their business. If the slaughtering businesses stopped picking up pigs, meat shops would inevitably purchase pigs from pig trades in Yangjing and Wusong (where pigs are delivered directly to the slaughterhouses without fees). The pig trade would not only have no business but also affect the release of their accounts. The leaders of the pig trade, including Xin Wenyao and Gu Bao, managers of Chunyuan and Changshun, personally went to the scene to strictly stop the pig stalls from collecting the "exit fee," stating that if they did not comply, the stalls would be taken back and operated independently. They also asked the slaughtering businesses to pick up pigs as usual. The slaughtering businesses, having long-standing relationships with the pig trade and unwilling to go too far, picked up pigs as usual under the supervision of the pig trade.

Representatives Sent to Petition: The entire city's slaughtering businesses believe that this so-called "exit fee," which is collected under false pretenses and without any obligation, is unaffordable. Although they are picking up pigs reluctantly under the pig trade's intervention, the issue may resurface if it is not formally abolished. Therefore, at 2:00 PM yesterday, they sent representatives Xu Jianzhang, Yu Huitang, Sun A'er, Shen A'er, Yu Bingkun, and others to petition the Municipal Government. They were received by Huang, a section member of the Second Section, who promised to notify the Bureau of Social Affairs to investigate. After the representatives left, they went to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to petition. They were received by Mr. Zhu Boyuan. After the representatives stated their intentions, Mr. Zhu promised to have the Business Section investigate and handle the matter. According to the representatives, the slaughtering businesses believe that this matter is of great importance to the future of their industry and have decided to oppose it to the end. They will also petition the Municipal Party Headquarters and issue a declaration today (the 25th), asking all sectors to uphold justice and stop the pig stalls' actions that are hindering the city's meat supply.

To Fulfill the Wishes of All Sectors to Promote National Products

Truck Accident on Fujian Road

At approximately 5:30 PM the day before yesterday, a truck from the Taiping Moving Company on Beijing Road was traveling north on Fujian Road when it rear-ended a rickshaw traveling on the left side of the road. The rickshaw overturned, and the rickshaw owner, Dr. Fang Juying, was seriously injured after being pinned under the vehicle. The truck ran over the rickshaw's springs and continued driving forward. The rickshaw puller chased after the truck, signaled the police to stop it, and detained it at the accident site. Police vehicle sent Dr. Fang to Renji Hospital for treatment. The truck driver was taken into custody at the police station for investigation. Dr. Fang's medical practice will be temporarily suspended to allow for recuperation.

Zhang Zhen's Retrial Verdict

Sentence Changed to Six Months Imprisonment

Lawyer Zhang Zhen (from Baoshan) graduated from Qunzhi University on Rue Robert. Last winter, Zhang Zhen's fraudulent behavior was detected by the victim, leading to a collective accusation. After investigation by the local court, the first instance verdict was delivered on February 28 of this year, sentencing Zhang Zhen to eight months imprisonment for fraud and imposing a fine of 400 yuan. Zhang refused to accept the verdict and appealed while in custody. The appeal was rejected. Zhang still refused to accept the verdict and appealed again to the Jiangsu High Court, which ordered a retrial. Judge Guan Liting held a hearing. The judge, considering Zhang's youth (24 years old this year), repeatedly guided him and gave him a chance to rehabilitate himself, ordering him to correct his past mistakes. The case was then concluded, awaiting pronouncement of the verdict. Details have been previously reported. It is now known that the case has been adjudicated. The original verdict regarding Zhang Zhen's crime and punishment and the confiscation order are rescinded. Zhang Zhen is sentenced to six months imprisonment for jointly forging documents and defrauding others of their property. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be credited against the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Fifteen forged seals of various sizes, thirty-two blank diplomas, twelve Qunzhi University diplomas with stubs, one hundred and fifty-three diploma stubs, and one Zhang Zhen lawyer's license are all confiscated.

Mr. Bao Jinpo, a prominent figure from Jiangxi, held a wedding ceremony for his fourth and fifth sons and Miss Xiangyin, daughter of Ma Dian, former Salt Transport Commissioner of Shandong, and Miss Yelian, daughter of Wang Huaichen, appraiser of the Administrative Court, yesterday at the Dachunghua Hotel on Xizang Road in this city. The brothers attended the same school and graduated at the same time, and the sisters-in-law attended the same school and married into the same family. Holding a joint wedding ceremony at the same time is a rare and grand occasion in Shanghai.

Publishing Circle

National Painting Monthly Sells Well Famous painters at sea, such as He Tianjian, Rui Binhong, Zheng Wuchang, Wang Yachen, Chen Xiaodie, Zhang Shanzi, Xie Gongzhan, etc., recently formed the Chinese Painting Association and published the National Painting Monthly, edited by He Tianjian. Two issues have been published. The Wangping Street Hanwen Zhengkai Printing Office and the Tianjin Dagong Daily Shanghai Branch on Ermalu Wangping Street are both selling it on consignment. Each issue is only sold for one dime. The content is rich and the copperplate illustrations are exquisite. The second issue has been published, with many works by various painters. Among them, Zheng Wuchang's "The Responsibility That Modern Chinese Painters Should Bear," Chen Xiaodie's "No Painting Theory in the Qing Dynasty," He Tianjian's "The Right and Wrong of Painting and Calligraphy Associations and Styles," Wang Yachen's "On Gu Kaizhi," and Huang Binhong's "Essentials of Painting Method" are especially enlightening and thought-provoking. Those engaged in Chinese painting should not miss it. More than ten illustrations are all masterpieces by painters of past dynasties, especially Qiu Shizhou's large imitation of Li Longmian's Qin Hui Tu, which is not commonly seen outside.

"My Views on Destiny" Published Xia Lei, from Yandang, Zhejiang, likes to study ancient Chinese philosophy. His recent book, "My Views on Destiny," is based on many ancient books and uses vernacular to explain the cycle of the five elements, mutual generation and restraint, and sixty-four kinds of changes in fate. It is quite interesting. The book is priced at fifty cents per copy and is sold on consignment at the Buddhist Bookstore on Jiaozhou Road in this city.

Heavily Revised Fourth Edition of the German Grammar Textbook, Later Volume This book was compiled and translated by Mr. Wang Zhuanzeng. The third edition was destroyed during the national crisis at the Baoshan Road Commercial Press main factory. This year, a certain army school in the capital adopted it as a textbook. Due to insufficient stock, it was illegally copied by a certain agency using lithography. Now, the translator has carefully revised and typeset a new edition. All advanced German class students can adopt it as a textbook. The price is still nine dimes. The former volume is being retypeset and will be the eighth revised edition. It is expected to be published before June of the 24th year. The library service department, as well as the Life Bookstore and the Author's Bookstore, are all selling it on consignment.

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor, I recently read in today's (December 24) news column of your newspaper that "At about 5:00 PM last night, the last bus No. 17 of the Huta Motor Company, traveling from Luodian Town to Shanghai Station, was ambushed by bandits at the north end of Dachang. Zhao Xiting, the director of the Liuhuo Huizhong Hospital, and the former director of the Dachang Public Security Bureau (now the director of the Baoshan First Public Security Bureau), etc., witnessed the bandits wearing gray uniforms." I took the 4:30 PM bus from Jiading to Shanghai at 4:15 PM that afternoon and arrived at Dachang, not the last bus from Luodian to Shanghai. I did not witness the above situation. I am writing to inform you and hope you will make corrections. Sincerely, Wu Zhen, Director of the Baoshan County First Public Security Bureau, December 24.

Dear Editor, I read in your newspaper's local news column on the 23rd of this month a news item entitled "Dyer Jumps from Building to Commit Suicide," which stated that "Wang Afu, a cashier from Shaoxing in the dye shop, secretly replaced inferior goods for petty gains, etc." Afu is a worker in the finishing department of the Lihe Dyeing Factory. Your newspaper mistakenly referred to him as a cashier in the dye shop, which concerns the reputation of all members of our association. We are writing to you to request that you make corrections. We look forward to it. Sincerely, Shanghai Dyeing Industry Vocational Union Silk and Satin Office, December 24.

Dear Editor, I read in your newspaper's local news section the story of the Immortal Fighting the Buddha Mother, a touching story of recognizing one's mother. It stated that the witness Li Jinzhang testified in court that he saw the defendant Lu Xiangtian assault the plaintiff Yu Hu. I live next door to Lu Xiangtian. At around 9:00 that day, I heard Yu Hu yelling and making noise upstairs, so I went to advise her. At that time, I saw Yu Hu scolding and making noise upstairs, while Lu Xiangtian was still downstairs. I went upstairs to advise her and saw Yu Hu scratching her face with her left hand in a fit of anger. I did not see Lu Xiangtian assault her. This fact has been stated clearly on record and there is no bias whatsoever. The report in your newspaper does not match the testimony I gave. I hereby request a correction to clarify the responsibility of a witness. Sincerely, Li Jinzhang, December 24.
