Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— By Zhang Henshui

Sixth Chapter The Poor Girl Is Not Ashamed to Teach, Treating the Western Teacher as Equal, Why Bother with Empty Humility

While Jia Duocai was thinking that, based on the point of touring the Zhou Mausoleum, he must talk about the situation in the Northwest. Unexpectedly, Mr. William changed the subject again. Seeing the Western-style book on the table with Chinese characters embossed in gold, he smiled and said, "Chinese characters are also very beautiful when written on books like this." As he said this, he pointed at the Western-style book with his fingers covered in yellow hair. Jia Duocai was even more confused. Such a conversation was simply like the kind of "the weather is very good today" greetings one would find in Chinese officialdom. He couldn't guess what these two had come for. William himself seemed to realize that his words were somewhat pointless, so he adopted a more serious demeanor and muttered something to Zhao Guofu. Judging from their expressions and eyes, it seemed that they were gradually getting to the main topic. So Jia Duocai also calmed down and listened to what they had to say. Zhao Guofu turned his face, first calling out "Mr. Jia," and then continued, "These two German gentlemen are managing German automobiles in China, and they are selling very well in the Northwest provinces. Mr. Jia, aren't you representing your bank in handling economic cooperation affairs in the Northwest? For example, buying grain, cotton, and the like, you always need automobiles for transportation. If you want to buy automobiles, our cars can be sold to you at an 80% discount." Hearing this, both Jia Duocai and Li Shilian understood. After all this commotion, it turned out that they were peddling business and selling. They hadn't come to visit scholars, let alone investigate the situation in the Northwest. Jia Duocai's careful arrangement and making a big deal out of a small issue was all in vain. Treating two car salesmen with such hospitality, even if no one knew, he still felt ashamed in his heart. He wasn't a poor person like Yueying, and he was free to feel embarrassed. He felt guilty before the gods, and his cheeks turned red. (98)

Art and Life

— Ma Foshēng

Zhao Zhiqian, courtesy name Huishu, his epigraphy, calligraphy, and painting are the authorities of the last hundred years. In recent times, only Wu Canglao of Anji can match him because he is known for his real skill and strength! Naturally, the so-called artists who specialize in taking shortcuts and lack real skill cannot hope to reach his level. He was from Dafangkou in Shaoxing City. One of his relatives used to help out at our house for a few days. We asked him to tell us stories about Huishu. According to him, Huishu had originally served as a county magistrate for a term. His epigraphy, calligraphy, and painting were simply his love and were not sold for money, so his works were very rare. At that time, it could truly be said that it was "art for art's sake." Later, because he was not used to bureaucratic flattery, he returned home and no longer served as an official (he had a seal engraved with "not bowing for five pecks of rice"), but his family was very poor and could only make a living through this. It changed to "art for life's sake." However, even so, he still refused to do it for money. He would only start when his wife had no rice to cook. If he had a satisfactory work, he would keep it for his own enjoyment and would not give it to others. Later, his family suffered a fire, and all the collected masterpieces were burned, so his works became even less common. I think that even a great master and artist of a generation was forced by life and could not adhere to his principle of "art for art's sake," and finally ended up with "art for life's sake." Perhaps the artists who are currently shouting loudly for "art for art's sake" may also not be defeated by life!

Snippets

— (Xing Guangyi Donates Remuneration to Aid Disaster Relief)

In this day and age, people follow each other's example, and everyone learns to be clever, thinking themselves clever and treating others as fools. But perhaps the fools will play tricks on the clever ones. Much of it is being clever for one's own sake, and the result is being misled by one's own cleverness.

This is called "hard to be confused."

Physiognomy

— Chánchén

Among my friends, there is one called Lao Wang. According to him, he knows everything about the three religions and nine streams, and he is especially good at the art of physiognomy. Although he cannot be compared to Tiangang Chunfeng, he can also be called a "semi-immortal with an iron mouth." When I first met him, he stared at my face with surprised eyes and exclaimed, "Brother, what a face you have! Especially your mouth, it can hold a fist, and you will definitely be rich in the future, but..." Then, he said in a regretful tone, "Unfortunately, there is a haze between your eyebrows, and your luck has not been very good in recent years." Finally, in a definite tone, he said decisively, "Three years from now, you will definitely soar, and then you will know the accuracy of my Lao Wang's physiognomy." After this, my heart was hot for a while, but I just smiled and dismissed it, not taking it seriously. Now, it has been five years since Lao Wang read my face, and I am still drifting in the world and as down on my luck as ever. Lao Wang's physiognomy has never been accurate.

After that, every time I saw him reading someone's face, it was always in this way: first praising or marveling at their appearance. Then regretting their current misfortune, and finally predicting that in a few years, they would definitely be rich or noble. As a result, the people who asked him to read their faces all left happily as if they had received supreme comfort.

Once, when we were drinking merrily, I asked him the secret of physiognomy. He talked eloquently, "Actually, there is nothing remarkable about my art of physiognomy. It's just a matter of remembering the three words 'surprise,' 'sigh,' and 'promise.' No matter who it is, if you praise them for their outstanding appearance, it will always be pleasing to the ear, so the first key to physiognomy is 'surprise,' because this can arouse people's interest. The second is 'sigh.' No matter whether you are successful or not, a person is always dissatisfied. I use this point to touch their hearts, regretting their current misfortune, so that they inevitably regret themselves. Then, my physiognomy has been successful in two-thirds. The final key is 'promise.' Since I have surprised and praised their appearance, and sighed at their misfortune, then I categorically promise that in a few years, they will definitely be rich and noble, giving them a beautiful and long-term check to cash, wouldn't that make them admire me wholeheartedly? Haha! This is the physiognomy secret that has been used for a long time and cannot be seen through."

Disturbance – Results Obtained in Previous Years

— Moon

The Floating Record of Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

I can't remember the location of this Fox Fairy Pagoda clearly, but it's probably in the northeast corner of Fengtian City. I hope this memory is correct, and even if it's wrong, it won't be too far off. However, I myself admit that I am not very good at recognizing directions. As soon as I get to a place that is relatively unfamiliar, I don't know which way is east and which way is west. Moreover, the streets in Fengtian City are very winding and difficult to recognize. Now that decades have passed, it is naturally not accurate to recall it!

Since the Empress Dowager's will to travel had been decided, orders were issued as usual to inform everyone to prepare. The first step was to send someone to the Fox Fairy Pagoda to drive away idlers to avoid disturbing the Empress Dowager's sacred presence. The second step was to select the route and lay yellow sand on every road that had to be passed to comply with the legal rules. Finally, a well-rehearsed team of honor guards set off in sequence.

I sat in the sedan chair and closed my eyes all the way, thinking carefully about why the myths that I had heard about in other ethnic groups were completely different from our Chinese myths? Whether it's true or false, there should be a reason. Unfortunately, I thought for a long time and couldn't figure it out. Perhaps scholars who specialize in mythology can answer it in a very organized way. I have always paid attention to mythology, but the passage that the Empress Dowager told us above did not arouse my special attention, but only felt very funny and ridiculous!

The procession always moved very slowly. Fortunately, none of us were sick and were not in a hurry to ask the Great Immortal for treatment. It didn't matter if we were slow! Finally, we arrived. (208)

(8) Statistics of Radio Households in Various Countries (1933)

United States: 17,005,000 households. United Kingdom: 5,263,000 households. Germany: 4,308,000 households. Japan: 1,348,000 households. Sweden: 609,000 households. Austria: 493,000 households. Belgium: 340,000 households. Italy: 305,000 households. Poland: 296,000 households. Spain: 100,000 households (End)

Little Common Sense

Common Knowledge About the Earth

— Bingyu

What exactly is the inside of the Earth, the land we stand on, like? Simply put, it is like the skin of an onion, composed of layers. Broadly speaking, the Earth can be divided into three layers: the outermost layer called the crust, the middle layer, and the core. The crust can be further divided into several layers. The ground we stand on is called the Sial layer. Below this layer is the Sima layer. The Sial layer is composed of rocks made of silicon and aluminum (metallic elements), chemically known as granite and quartz. The Sima layer is made of silicon and magnesium (metallic elements), forming basalt, which is a basic rock. The crust is about 1,200 kilometers thick.

The middle layer, located beneath the crust, can also be divided into two layers: the upper layer is the Chrome-Sima layer, composed of silicon, iron, magnesium, chromium, and other elements; the lower layer is the Silicate-Sima layer, also composed of iron, nickel, silicon, magnesium, and other elements. The middle layer is about 1,700 kilometers thick. This layer is similar to meteorites that fall from the sky.

As for the core, it is called the Nickel-Iron layer, composed of nickel. Some say this layer is a rigid body, very hard, while others say it is a liquid, similar to water. However, no one has been able to drill to the center of the Earth, so we cannot definitively determine what it is like. However, based on observations during earthquakes and studies of tidal phenomena, the center of the Earth must be harder than mud. It is likely a rigid solid.

The ratio of the weight of the Earth's crustal rocks to the specific gravity of the Earth is 2.67 to 5.22. Geologists have found that the specific gravity of the Sima layer is 2.8 to 3.4, the Chrome-Sima layer is 4, the Silicate-Sima layer is 5.6, and the Nickel-Iron layer is 6.2. Those with some knowledge of physics and chemistry will understand this theory.

But how is the Earth's interior divided? Let's use a kitchen knife as an analogy to cut the Earth into two pieces (this is a metaphor, like cutting an apple or an onion, because there is no knife large enough to dissect the Earth). Let me explain. You have probably heard of doctors using X-rays to examine the source of diseases in the body's internal organs. This is similar to how geologists examine the Earth's interior. Although they cannot drill into the Earth, they can study it theoretically, as if it were a transparent glass ball, which they can see very clearly. These scholars use precise seismographs to observe earthquakes (ground movements). For example, when a major earthquake occurs in San Francisco, they can calculate the time it takes for the vibration to travel from the Earth's interior to various places. They can predict when the earthquake will reach Beijing or Shanghai with great accuracy. Those without knowledge might call them gods. In fact, for those who have studied astronomy extensively, it is quite simple. Look at the weather forecasts from the Shanghai Xujiahui Observatory. How do they predict whether it will be sunny tomorrow or rainy the day after? It's the same principle.

Geologists can infer from the Earth's layers that there are points between 60 kilometers and 1,200 kilometers below the surface where the density of rocks changes significantly. Also, the density from the surface to a depth of 2,900 kilometers is very different. The first point of difference is the boundary between the Sima layer and the Sial layer. The second point is the boundary between the Sima layer and the middle layer. The third point is the boundary between the middle layer and the Nickel-Iron layer.

The temperature of the Sima layer below the Sial layer is very high, and the pressure is also great. According to ordinary temperature calculations, the center of the Earth has tens of thousands of degrees (geologists estimate between 5,000 and 6,000 degrees Celsius) and a pressure of over 2 million atmospheres. With such a high temperature inside the Earth, the entire Earth has twice the rigidity of iron. Earthquake waves pass through the Earth's interior, and the gravity of the sun and moon causes changes in the Earth's surface water, creating tides. From this, we can infer that the Earth's interior is composed of highly elastic materials.

The Capital Will Open a Research Institute for Administrative Personnel of the Mongolian Leagues and Banners

The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission submitted a request to prepare for the establishment of a Research Institute for Administrative Personnel of the Mongolian Leagues and Banners and drafted an outline of the organization of the Research Institute. The request was submitted to the Executive Yuan, which instructed the four ministries of Interior, Finance, Military Affairs, and Education, as well as the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and the General Staff Headquarters, to send personnel to participate in a joint review of the outline of the organization of the Research Institute and report to the Executive Yuan for submission to the Yuan Council for amendment and approval. The Executive Yuan has instructed the ministries to be informed. Now that the outline and budget of the Research Institute have been approved, it can be opened in the capital in the spring. The main points of the revised outline of the organization of the Research Institute are summarized below: (1) The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission has specially established the Research Institute for Administrative Personnel of the Mongolian Leagues and Banners in order to improve the administrative efficiency of the Mongolian Leagues and Banners. (2) This institute is directly under the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and is located in the capital. (3) The qualifications and number of researchers in this institute shall be in accordance with the following regulations: 1. Each Mongolian league and department shall send one incumbent staff member of the rank of participating leader or above. 2. Each Mongolian flag's Zhasake or director (if the Zhasake or director cannot leave their position, they may each send one incumbent staff member of the rank of participating leader or above). (4) The research period is limited to six months. During the research period in Beijing, the researcher's original position and salary shall be retained. After the research period expires, they shall return to their original position. Those with excellent performance may be given priority for promotion. (5) Research subjects: (1) Party Doctrine, (2) Outline of Administration, (3) Current Mongolian Laws and Regulations, (4) Outline of History and Geography, (5) National Language and Literature, (6) Outline of Animal Husbandry, (7) Outline of Hygiene, (8) Common Agricultural Knowledge, (9) Spiritual Lectures, (10) Current Administrative Organization, (11) Other subjects deemed necessary (omitted below).

Anhui Reorganization Education Conference Opens

(Anhui News) The Anhui Provincial Reorganization Local Education Conference was held at the old site of the Education Department in the auditorium at 2 PM on December 20th. Attendees included Acting Chairman Ma of the Provincial Government, Director of Finance Mao Longzhang, Director of Education Yang Lian, Experts Xie Xunchu, Hao Zhaochu, Luo Jilin, etc., as well as principals of provincial secondary schools and directors of provincial social education institutions, and more than 70 county education directors. Guests included Xiong Wenqin, Chairman of the National Military Training Association, and Jiang Wei, a scribe from the Gazetteer Hall. Chairman Yang Lian and Vice Chairman Zheng Hecun first reported the purpose of the meeting, saying roughly that Anhui Province's local education is far inferior to that of other places with good results, and recently there is even the suffering of having no way out. Anhui Province's local education funds originally totaled 2.3 to 4 million yuan, but this year's drought has reduced them by 6 to 700,000 yuan, and the abolition of harsh and miscellaneous taxes will reduce them by another 5 to 600,000 yuan, a total reduction of half. 70% of the 2.2 million elementary school students will drop out of school. Now we need to discuss: 1. How to make up for the funding gap, 2. How to prevent children from suffering from dropping out of school, 3. How to integrate productive education with compulsory education, 4. How to test the methods that are currently being tested or have achieved results in various provinces and cities. After the report, Chairman Ma gave instructions, and Director Mao and Xunchu gave speeches, followed by a reply from Zhou Zhenhua, a representative of the members. The meeting adjourned at 4 PM. At 6 PM, the provincial government hosted a banquet for all members, and the provincial party department also scheduled a reception for all members.

Student National Goods Year Opening Meeting Yesterday, Various Groups Initiated

Revised Organizational Outline, Formally Appointed Directors

Preparing for the Opening Ceremony on New Year's Day Next Year

The Student National Goods Year, initiated and prepared by educational and commercial circles in this city, held an inaugural meeting of various groups at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA at 3:00 PM yesterday. The meeting revised the organizational outline, formally appointed directors, and discussed preparations for the New Year's Day opening ceremony. Details are recorded as follows:

List of Participating Groups: Present were Pan Gongzhan from the Municipal Education Bureau, Wang Longzhang and Huang E from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Peng Zhenqiu from the Social Affairs Bureau, Huang Zaoxiong from the Municipal Education Office, Zhang Taoyong from the University Federation, Kang Xuanyi from the University Education Federation, Chen Jicheng from the Middle School Education Federation, Zheng Xigu from the Middle School Advancement Association, Yu Zuoting and Zheng Chengqing from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Zhu Xuefan and Long Peiyun from the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, Huang Renzhi from the Municipal Local Association, Lin Kecong from the Municipal Women's Association, Pan Yangyao from the Vocational Education Society, Chen Yiting from the Promote National Goods Association, Fang Yexian from the China National Development and Sales Association, Yu Xinyi from the Daily Newspaper Association, Sun Daosheng from the Journalists Association, Sun Choucheng from the National Goods Factory Federation, Wu Shuxing from the China General Industry Association, Wu Zhihao from the Shanghai National Goods Company, Huang Bingpei from the Family Renewal Society, Hua Wanruo from the Women's National Development Association, and over fifty people including Ren Jinpin and Yang Jiaoqi.

Chairman's Opening Remarks: Chairman Pan Gongzhan, Recorder Ren Jinpin. The chairman first delivered a speech, saying, "The initiation of this Student National Goods Year is because, considering the national goods movement since its implementation last year and this year being the Women's National Goods Year, it has achieved considerable success. Although some people believe that import and export trade has a yearly deficit, they think the national goods movement is still ineffective. Others believe that this year is the Women's National Goods Year, yet the import of cosmetics is astonishing, further leading them to believe that the national goods movement has no effect at all. However, they do not realize that if there had been no enthusiastic people promoting and implementing national goods in the past two years, the import deficit of foreign goods would probably have been even worse. Furthermore, the increased quantity of import deficits in recent years should not be attributed to the lack of effort by those engaged in the national goods movement. For example, the surge in gasoline imports due to the construction of domestic highways is one instance. Although the quantity of imported cosmetics has increased recently, the flourishing success of national cosmetics today is undoubtedly due to the efforts of the women's community in promoting national goods. Therefore, the national goods movement is better to do than not to do, and better to put in effort than not to put in effort. With this in mind, colleagues have scheduled next year as the Student National Goods Year, because students are pure and youthful, with great power of action. By setting an example and awakening compatriots, the effect will surely increase," and so on.

Discussion of Important Matters: After the chairman's speech, Chen Jicheng reported on the preparatory process. Then, the proposals were discussed: (1) Proposal to determine the name: It was resolved to name it the "Student National Goods Year Promotion Federation." (2) Proposal to determine the organizational outline: It was resolved to revise and approve it. (3) Proposal to determine the work outline: It was resolved to revise and approve it. (4) Proposal to appoint directors and conveners of the board of directors: It was resolved to formally approve the list and elect Pan Gongzhan, Fang Yexian, Wu Zhihao, Zhang Shouyong, and Yu Zuoting as conveners. (5) Proposal for preparations for the New Year's Day opening ceremony: It was resolved to entrust it to the preparatory committee. (6) Proposal to raise funds: It was resolved that the two major Shanghai Chinese national goods companies would temporarily advance 500 yuan as preparatory funds. (7) Proposal to elect the presidium for the opening ceremony: It was resolved to elect twelve people, with the list recorded separately. After the discussion, tea and refreshments were served, and the meeting adjourned.

Revised Organizational Outline: The revised organizational outline of the Student National Goods Year Promotion Federation is as follows: (1) This association is jointly initiated by educational and commercial groups. Based on the year's theme of the national goods movement, it is named the "Student National Goods Year Promotion Federation." (2) The purpose of this association is to promote the inherent patriotic spirit of students, awaken the public to use national goods, and unite with commercial and industrial circles to work together to promote the national goods movement. (3) Members of this association are schools, national goods factories, national goods stores, and organizations enthusiastic about national goods. Each joining member will send one to two representatives. (4) Membership fees for this association are voluntarily contributed by each member. (5) This association will have a board of directors, whose members will be appointed by public agreement of the initiating groups. The board of directors will decide to appoint committee members from the designated representatives to form the following committees: 1. School Committee; 2. National Factory Committee; 3. National Goods Store Committee; 4. Economic Committee; 5. Design Committee; 6. Publicity Committee. The School Committee may establish branches within each school. 7. This association may hire staff as needed to carry out the intentions of the board of directors, serving the various committees. 8. The regulations for the board of directors and various committees of this association will be established separately. 9. Matters not covered in this outline may be added, deleted, or modified by the board of directors.

Revised Work Outline: The revised work outline of the Student National Goods Year Promotion Federation is as follows: 1. Realize the objectives of the Student National Goods Year; 2. Assist school members in holding publicity gatherings; 3. Assist national factories in improving production quality and increasing production quantity; 4. Assist national goods stores in promoting national goods; 5. Assist each member in establishing national goods promotion agencies; 6. Report to each member monthly on the customs situation for the year, including a comparison with the same month last year.

Preparing for the New Year's Day Opening: The Student National Goods Year Promotion Federation has decided to hold the opening ceremony on New Year's Day next year in the auditorium of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The preparatory committee has already begun preparations. The presidium of the conference has been elected by the initiating conference of various groups, including Pan Gongzhan, Tong Xingbai, Yu Zuoting, Fang Yexian, Wu Zhihao, Zhang Shouyong, Huang Renzhi, Zhu Xuefan, Zheng Xigu, Lin Kecong, Huang Bingpei, and Tang Guanyu, totaling twelve people.

Special Article

German Secondary School Teacher Training (II)

Zhu Zhen Sun

(II) Methods of Secondary School Teacher Training

Regarding German secondary school teacher training, teachers can be divided into two types. The first type is teachers of general subjects who have graduated from universities or higher vocational schools. The second type is teachers of special subjects such as physical education, art, and applied art. The training received by these teachers is lower than that received by teachers from universities, and in terms of remuneration and priority, they only hold a secondary position in secondary schools. The main force in German secondary schools is mostly occupied by the first type of teachers, so we will take this type of teacher as the object of our research.

Unlike other European countries, Germany does not have a national education ministry. Germany is a federal state composed of sixteen organizations, and they have autonomy over education, judicial administration, and certain taxation. However, they all abide by the provisions of the national constitution promulgated on August 11, 1919. However, the autonomous education departments of all federal states are now completely consistent with the imperial education department established in 1871. Therefore, secondary school diplomas are still valid throughout Germany, as are university degrees. The curriculum, academic programs, and teaching process of secondary education are uniform everywhere, so they can be used for a kind of exchange class (Kassenauslausch) experiment. This alternating class experiment is that students from secondary schools in different cities in Germany (such as Munich and Hamburg) can exchange classes. For example, students from academic or science-based secondary schools in Munich can study for several weeks under the guidance of teachers from similar secondary schools in Hamburg, and students from schools in Hamburg can similarly study in similar schools in Munich. This method does not prejudice the academic progress of ordinary students because the level of work in each secondary school is very uniform.

Regarding the selection and training methods of German secondary school teachers, for the convenience of discussion, it is best to take Prussia as the standard. The training of secondary school teachers in Prussia is stipulated by national examinations. This national examination consists of two parts: 1. Degree examination; 2. Teacher examination.

1. Degree examination: This examination is organized in accordance with the decrees of the Prussian Education Ministry of July 27, 1917, January 2, 1926, January 19, 1927, October 15, and February 4, 1930. The following are the necessary conditions for candidates:

(1) Secondary school diploma

(2) Eight semesters of study at a German university, three of which must be at a Prussian university.

(3) In addition to taking major and minor subjects at the university, candidates must also attend lectures in philosophy and education.

(4) Candidates must have personally participated in practical physical exercises for two semesters and received two semesters of physical education lectures.

This examination is presided over by a special committee designated by the Education Ministry. All committee members are mostly professors from universities and secondary education experts. The position of chairman is often held by secondary education experts. The chairman of the examination committee is legally empowered to make decisions, and he decides whether to allow candidates to participate in the examination. He can reject the request of any candidate whose conditions do not meet the regulations. The chairman's decision can only be vetoed by the Minister of Education.

The examination subjects are divided into ordinary and special subjects. The special subjects are designated by the candidates themselves. These special subjects are divided into three types: two major and one minor. Candidates can choose two major subjects from the following: Christian doctrine, German, Latin, Greek, French, English, history, geography, mathematics, physics, chemistry, botany, and zoology. Candidates can choose one minor subject from the following: Introduction to philosophy, political science, education, applied mathematics, geology, mineralogy, history of medieval and modern art, comparative linguistics, Polish, Swiss, Russian, Spanish, Italian, Turkish, Dutch, religious history, and Chinese.

There are two methods of examination: written and oral. The written examination is divided into two types: 1. Writing two essays; 2. On-site examination. As for the two essays, there are also major and minor distinctions. The topic of the major essay is selected from the candidate's major subjects, and the topic of the minor essay is selected from the minor subject. Candidates have five months to prepare for the major essay and three months to prepare for the minor essay. With the permission of the chairman of the examination committee, the preparation time for the major essay can be increased by six weeks, and the preparation time for the minor essay can be increased by four weeks. If the examination committee believes that the candidate's essay has special and profound value, he can be exempted from all or part of the on-site examination. The examination time is set at three hours. During the examinations between 1929 and 1930, among the 872 candidates, 92 were exempted from all on-site written examinations due to the special value of their essays.

The oral examination is conducted separately by another committee. This committee consists of at least three people, namely the chairman, the examiner, and the recorder. The recorder's duty is to record the candidate's answers in detail. The results of each examination are indicated by four grades: excellent, upper, middle, and lower. If a subject is failed, the candidate can apply for a makeup examination. The method of makeup examination is determined by the committee. Applicants for makeup examinations should pay a makeup examination fee of eight marks. Those who pass the examination can obtain a secondary school teacher's degree. (To be continued)

Free Talk

"Selected Works"

— Zai Qing

In the "Society Talk" section of "Literature," there was a short essay "On Selected Works," explaining the disarray and repetition of current selected works, and hoping that those who select books would explore new paths and not just spin around in this narrow circle. This opinion is completely correct. In the article "On Essays Selection" (Literary Landscape), I once referred to such books as "selected works of selected works." Now that I think about it, I feel that I have to add a little explanation, that is, it does not mean "more carefully selected," but rather arbitrarily selecting from selected works, putting together a miscellaneous book, and fundamentally there is no "selection."

Selected works are a big deal, and they are also more effective and more immortal than individual collections. Many collections of writings can be lost, but good selected works are often not easily destroyed. The reason is: selected works concentrate the essence of each author's works, allowing readers to understand more things with less economic expense and less time. But such selected works are definitely not of the kind of "arbitrarily selected, putting together a miscellaneous book." Therefore, the benefits of selected works are many, if the selector is excellent and willing to treat selecting books as a career and do it carefully.

The pity is that there are not many such selectors, so that "speculative and shoddy" selected works often appear on the market. That is why people who buy books select and select in the pile of selected works, but in the end they cannot select anything. The reason for this phenomenon is not simple. There is a relationship with the development of the printing industry, the business sense of publishers, and also the lives of selectors. Under various complex conditions, it is impossible to eliminate this phenomenon. The only way to remedy this is to painstakingly put in the effort to criticize and select selected works, and constantly supervise and liquidate. This responsibility should be borne by critics.

There is a very bad trend in the Chinese publishing industry, which is that it is unwilling to develop in different directions, and often jointly bites the same book, desperately fighting, and will not stop until both sides are injured. For example, the "Twenty-Four Histories," "Twenty-Five Histories," and "Twenty-Six Histories" are examples of this. Therefore, if publisher A makes a profit from a selection of essays, publisher B will also make another one, and publisher C will be a little envious and add one to join in the fun. If this continues to develop, it will inevitably lead to everyone selling essays, everyone buying essays, and even if it is not an essay, it will be forcibly counted as an essay, and China will be made into an essay country. There is definitely no situation where you publish the "Complete Works of Yuan Zhonglang" and I do not print it, but print the collection of another person. The publishing of selected works is so bad and the scope is so narrow. This trend in the publishing industry is, I think, a big reason. The publisher's demand for "production machinery" is so high, and the selector is forced by life to adapt to the other party's demands, which is very impossible. I hope that selectors can develop new paths, and at the same time, I have to hope that publishers can change this bad trend.

On the Riverbank (Continued)

— Mo Fu

"There must be a village ahead!"

Finally, in the dim moonlight, we spotted some dark shapes and shouted out in surprise. As we drew closer, barking dogs grew louder, confirming our guess. Our spirits lifted, and our breathing became easier.

In reality, it wasn't much of a village, just a few scattered thatched huts. Trees were scarce, and there was hardly a street to be seen. The dogs barked more fiercely, but it was a monotonous sound, revealing the small number of residents in the village. Was there an inn? Which one was it? We were worried about how to solve this problem because we were strangers in the middle of the night.

"This is an inn!"

Suddenly, a companion standing in front of a large door shouted joyfully, showing a liveliness he hadn't had before. I almost felt like jumping for joy. We started shouting loudly and pounded on the faded, peeling black oil door with our hands and feet. But no matter how hard we tried, it remained quiet inside, with no response, which made us anxious. Most of our companions sat on their luggage, heads drooping, feeling helpless. But were we willing to give up? After a while, we started knocking again.

"Who is it?" Suddenly, a rough voice asked.

"Guests! Open the door quickly!"

We stopped knocking, and there was no more sound from inside. So, one by one, we pleaded towards the door, explaining how we had crossed the river, why we couldn't enter the wharf, where we had landed, and so on. Unexpectedly, we heard a sound of "hmm" from inside the door. As the door opened, an elderly man with a sallow face and a beard appeared. He was stunned by the sight of our group of people. Naturally, I couldn't wait for him to ask any questions, so we crowded in.

The courtyard was spacious. On the left was a row of factory buildings, with troughs for feeding livestock. At one end, several animals were munching on grass. Two carters emerged from under the factory building, their sheepskin blankets draped loosely over their shoulders, and asked us about our journey in a nasal, mumbled way.

The old man with the beard reappeared and, as the innkeeper, led us into a three-room empty house lit by a dim kerosene lamp.

Only then did we regain our composure, shake off our fears, and feel the gnawing pain of our long-empty stomachs. "Snacks? We're starving."

"Innkeeper, hot water!"

Suddenly, the empty house became lively. To warm up, the innkeeper started boiling water in the house. While munching on food, everyone talked loudly about what they had seen, felt, and imagined on the riverbank, their faces showing a unique joy after the initial shock. Every time they talked about something frightening, they couldn't help but tighten their lips and widen their eyes.

I sat in front of the fire, staring blankly at the old man boiling water, recalling the experience of crossing the river. The most terrifying part wasn't my own timidity and self-frightening, but the arrow-like rapids, the roaring of the angry waves against the riverbank, the helplessness of being unable to escape on horseback, and the precariousness of traveling on a broken wooden boat along the riverbank, with the possibility of death at any moment. At that moment, I truly understood the saying "The farther you go across the Yellow River, the more afraid you become." (The End)

The "Origin" of a Buddhist Image Emerging from a Clam Shell

— Xiao Shuxuan

After Mr. Chen Zizhan's "Buddhist Image Emerging from a Clam Shell" was published, Mr. Jiang Hongyi provided a "scientific explanation," and Mr. A Ying collected materials. Thus, it is evident that this article has attracted some attention. Those unaware that the Buddhist image in the clam shell "is artificially crafted" naturally find it strange (see Mr. Chen's "Postscript" in the 5th issue). However, its shadow cannot escape the eyes of folklorists! We can see Mr. Chen's emphasis on this matter and his "textual research" in his repeated postscripts. But since he insists on researching whether it "has an origin" (see "Buddhist Image Emerging from a Clam Shell" in the October 4th issue), I will also bring up some "dead people" (historical sources).

Yang Yu's "New Talks from a Mountain Dwelling" mentions that Emperor Wenzong of Yuan liked to eat clams and saw a Bodhisattva image inside one. Mr. Chen suspects that this refers to Emperor Wenzong of Yuan; the "Records of the Transmission of the Lamp" says it was Emperor Wenzong of Tang. However, since Yang Yu states that Emperor Wenzong "placed the clam image in a sandalwood box and presented it to Xing'an Temple, ordering respect for it," we can compare it with what Tang's Grand Master Duan Chengshi said in "Miscellanies from Youyang, Continued":

"In Jingshan Ward, the Daxing'an Temple... Looking to the left: there is a clam image, traditionally said to be from the time of the Sui Emperor, who was fond of clams and consumed them in countless numbers. Suddenly, one clam was struck as usual, but the Emperor found it strange. He placed it on the table, and overnight it shone brightly. By morning, the meat had separated, and inside was an image of a Buddha and two Bodhisattvas. The Emperor was filled with remorse and vowed never to eat clams again!!" (Volume 5, Record of Temples and Pagodas)

Doesn't this say that the Xing'an Temple still had the clam image during the Tang Dynasty? Although it doesn't explicitly say that the Sui Emperor "presented it to Xing'an Temple," historically, the construction of temples and pagodas was most flourishing during the reign of Emperor Wen of Sui. Therefore, this question can be answered quite appropriately. Furthermore, this shows that the origin of the clam image dates back to Emperor Wen of Sui! It originated as early as the Sui Dynasty! In the same volume, Chengshi also includes a twenty-character couplet about the clam image, which mentions "a sacred pillar with traces of iron chains." I wonder if this refers to the "sacred pillar" in Xing'an Temple? Perhaps it can be found in the "Records of Buddhist Temples in Jinling," but unfortunately, I don't have that book at hand and cannot investigate it further.

Regarding the origin of this matter, the Sui Dynasty is undoubtedly the earliest, but it cannot be said to be its true source, as it is related to the superstition of animal worship. The manifestation of the divine in animals also carries a didactic meaning. However, on the other hand, it is the result of the clam itself being regarded as a sacred and extraordinary object. In the "Monthly Ordinances of the Book of Rites," it says, "In the month of late winter, pheasants enter the great water and become mirages." The "mirage" is a large clam, which is also a shellfish. Guo Pu of the Jin Dynasty commented on the Erya dictionary, saying, "A shellfish is a mirage." Xing Bing of the Song Dynasty explained, "A mirage is a large clam" (Annotations and Explanations of Fish in the Erya Dictionary). Shellfish and clams were originally the same thing, differing only in size and name. Moreover, it's not just that "pheasants become mirages, and sparrows become shellfish" (from the "Discussion on Immortals" in the Baopuzi; due to space limitations, I cannot elaborate further here). Gao You's commentary on the Huainanzi also mentions, "The Fangzhu is a large clam. If you rub it until it is hot and face it towards the moon, water will be generated," which is quite mysterious! Thus, it became a tool in Taoist naturalistic theories; thus, it became related to the alchemy of the alchemists; and thus, during the Ming Dynasty, there were records of images of the Eight Immortals, the God of Longevity, etc., appearing in clam shells (see Zheng Zhongkui's "Junque").

Fine Wine and Women

Coming from Volcano Master (4)

— Lan Ru

"Ah... It's really hard to walk! The sand has filled my feet." They had all arrived, chatting and giggling. Upon their reminder, I realized that my shoes were also full of sand. I thought about sitting down to empty them, but then I realized that my feet would just fill up with sand again, so why bother wasting the effort.

Indeed, only now did I truly feel that life in the desert was too difficult! The vast desert stretched out before you, with not a single tree, blade of grass, or bird in sight. My throat was so parched it felt like it was on fire, yet there was no way to find a drop of water in the desert. I deeply regretted not eating all the fruit earlier, as it would have been such a joy to use it to quench my thirst now.

Each step sank into the sand, covering your legs. You had to exert all your strength to pull your feet out and take another step, but every step was just as difficult, just as impossible to drag your feet forward.

Thus, pain and annoyance arose!

Watching the ant-like crowd winding their way across the mountain ridge, I envied their ability to walk while I couldn't catch up, a wish unfulfilled. But the sand seemed to deliberately make things difficult for you. The more you wanted to walk faster, the more your feet were buried in the sand, unable to be pulled out. What made you even more anxious was the northerly wind, as sharp as scissors, constantly blowing. Countless fine grains of sand stung your face like hailstones—no, almost like shrapnel. Eyes, nostrils, ears... sand was everywhere. Your hair was completely covered in sand, and as you walked, it scattered down like sand snow.

I was now breathless and could no longer catch up with them, often stopping involuntarily. Several times I fell onto the sand, losing consciousness as if I had developed a tumor. Mr. Qin, waiting impatiently ahead, desperately urged us forward with his stick. My spirit was so exhausted that I couldn't lift my feet anymore. But my mind was still clear. It told me that stopping here was absolutely impossible, that the journey back was even longer than going forward, and that we hadn't even seen the volcano yet. I was determined not to give up.

Mount Yilie

— Shi Dai

"Rolling the Ball of Silk."

"Let's go! Let's go see 'Rolling the Ball of Silk'!"

Many people were shouting, drawn by the strange spectacle towards Mount Yilie. Children were also eagerly moving their hands and feet, wanting to see this rare "once-in-a-century" event; however, the adults stopped these children, even though they cried and wailed, they were not allowed to go there! The children struggled frantically, resulting in the adults locking them up in the yurt, where they continued to cry and make noise.

Everyone understood that the death penalty of "Rolling the Ball of Silk" was the most cruel! This cruelty not only inflicted terrible suffering on the prisoner, but also caused pain in the hearts of the viewers! Children's minds are fragile, and it would be dangerous if they were exposed to such stimulation!

The sky was covered in thick clouds, frighteningly gloomy, and the sun was hidden behind them. A wind, having turned from wild to sharp, pricked at the skin and bones. The reflection of the snow illuminated the sky, turning the dense clouds a grayish-white color, swirling and preparing to scatter snowflakes onto the earth.

The vast plains, the towering mountains, and the yurt-like mounds were all dressed in pure white.

The crowd wriggled on the snow, looking like fly droppings on a white tablecloth from afar, little by little. They walked, walking quickly. The white Mount Yilie was already packed with dark figures.

The prisoner's arms were tied behind him, and he leaned crookedly on the snow. His face was devoid of color, his eyes glazed over, and his lips were dry and almost gone.

"He's quite young!" someone said.

More and more people gathered, each pushing aside the shoulders and arms of others, clearing their line of sight. It seemed that at this moment, everyone had forgotten the cold.

"What did he do to commit such a crime?"

It was the old man from Lasar Island asking someone.

After a long pause, a young man replied:

"He stole twenty horses from King Sayan!"

"How bold! Daring to steal King Sayan's livestock!"

Various discussions emerged from the people's mouths, only whispered private discussions, with fear jumping in everyone's heart.

A commotion began as a large group of people climbed up from the foot of the mountain. King Sayan, wearing a shiny purple robe and a face-illuminating yellow jacket, walked majestically to the top of the mountain.

"Clear the way! Clear the way!"

The mounted guards with guns shouted loudly, clearing the crowd.

King Sayan dismounted, and the guards swarmed around him. A guard with a pockmarked face went to drag the prisoner to King Sayan. The prisoner was like a dead pig, not moving or making a sound.

Before long, King Sayan clasped his hands together and held the Buddhist rosary, announcing the prisoner's crimes to everyone:

"Irat Ussuri is a very bad person. He doesn't believe in the sky god Chao Ma! He doesn't keep to his duties and steals other people's livestock everywhere! He even dared to steal my livestock! The 'Living Buddha' told me that this person must be punished with 'Rolling the Ball of Silk'! Otherwise, the people of our Kuku Plain will not be able to live in peace!"

Everyone seemed not to have heard King Sayan's words, scanning the dying prisoner Irat Ussuri with eyes hiding fear.

"Do it!"

The shout came from King Sayan's mouth. The guards rudely tied a long, round blue stone weighing a hundred or so pounds to the prisoner's body with a leather rope, then ruffled the prisoner's hair and poured some kerosene on it. King Sayan shouted:

"Release!"

Then, the pockmarked man lit the oil on the prisoner's hair with a torch, causing flames to rise. Two people came over, lifted the prisoner forcefully, and threw him down the mountain with all their might! Flames flickered as the prisoner's body tumbled straight from the mountaintop to the bottom of the mountain. King Sayan laughed heartily and triumphantly mounted his chestnut horse.

A sense of desolation enveloped the hearts of every spectator, leaving traces of pity on their faces. The old man from Lasar Ude wiped his tears and patted a middle-aged man beside him, saying:

"Pray to the Living Buddha for protection! We must not break the law!"

The middle-aged man lowered his head, thinking about the changes in this tragic scene. He seemed not to have heard the old man's words.

The sky was gloomy, and the air was stagnant! Sadness hung on people's faces as they dejectedly walked down Mount Yilie.

Irat Ussuri's corpse lay stiff on the snow, the white snow smeared with red blood, the ropes broken. The face was a bloody mess, and it was no longer possible to distinguish the nose from the mouth.

Cocoon (4)

— Original by Hayashi Fusao, translated by Shizuko

Sakai's mother, a woman with quiet, old-fashioned eyebrows, spoke in a very kind tone, repeatedly saying how much Yūichi had always been in his care and asking for his continued support in the future, while bowing her already graying head in front of me. Embarrassed and ashamed, my face flushed red, I just nodded repeatedly, not daring to look directly at Sakai's mother's face, which expressed elegance and humility.

On the way home from the factory, Sakai told me about his experiences in a very quiet tone. His father had died when he was in the fourth grade of elementary school, leaving behind his mother and him. Since his father's death, their once reasonably comfortable family had completely fallen apart. For several years, they had relied solely on his mother's hands to raise him. To send him to middle school, his mother had become a factory worker in a silk mill. Although he stubbornly refused to go to middle school, the teachers at school all advised that it would be a pity to drop out halfway, and his mother said that he was the only one who could revive the Sakai family. Such tearful pleadings had led him to start school. However, to pay the tuition, his mother had no choice but to wear down her aging body in such an unhealthy factory. He didn't want to go to school at all. His mother's monthly wage was barely enough to cover his tuition, but if he dropped out, it would disappoint his mother, who was working with a full heart of hope. So, partly out of necessity and partly out of gratitude, he was attending school.

"I have never told anyone about this. Nor is there any need to tell anyone. But you—only you—are very dear to me. I often talk about you with my mother, and she always says, while shedding tears, that she wants to meet you and thank you, no matter what. That's why I invited you here today."

".................................................................................................."

"Also," Sakai continued immediately, "there is another reason why I took you to that factory. Perhaps you have already noticed. The owner of that factory is the father of Ōkawa, the man I stabbed with a knife before."

"Ah," I nodded.

"Therefore, I think what I did before was not very good. It is, of course, despicable to bully the weak without reason, but it is also cowardly to retaliate with personal feelings. If Ōkawa hadn't been in that group—if Ōkawa, who mocked my mother for working in his factory, hadn't been there—I wouldn't have drawn my knife. By the time I realized it, I couldn't help but cry at my own cowardice."

I gazed at the blood-red sunset slowly sinking into the sea from the top of the street houses, listening quietly to his words as I watched.

Two or three years passed.

We were both now students at a higher school. Sakai had received a scholarship from the prefecture, and I had somehow passed the entrance exam without incident.

Commercial News

Financial Leverage Loosens, Gold Standard Premium Drops Another $2.90

Currency Market Stiffens, Trading Loosens

Daily Situation: Easier to Fall Than Rise

Since last Saturday, after the Kwong group vigorously sold gold bars, the gold market's leverage loosened yesterday, making it easier to fall than rise. The currency market also stiffened, retreating into the $80 range before stabilizing with scattered transactions. Early morning, overseas silver markets saw slight rebounds in both London and New York, with forward silver prices also rising and exchange rates slightly increasing. London spot gold fell 2.5 pence, reflecting a slight rebound in sentiment after last Saturday's sharp decline. Off-exchange pre-market trading opened higher at $88.80, but due to eager supply at higher prices, it gradually declined. The Central Bank's official exchange rates were announced, with the British pound unchanged and the U.S. dollar up $0.0625. Customs gold units contracted 2.5 pence, and the listed standard price for the gold premium retreated to $1013.20. The morning opening was still high, initially appearing stable, but then softened due to the loosening currency market and oversupply in the market. The Central Bank and others took advantage of lower prices to cover their positions. The Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) kept its British and American exchange rates unchanged. Afterwards, it turned from stable to firm, rising briefly. Yarn Exchange Will Close for Four Days for New Year Holidays

The Shanghai Yarn and Cloth Exchange market announced that, as the national New Year's Day is approaching, the Exchange will stop bidding from December 31, 23rd year of the Republic, and will be closed in accordance with regulations until the normal business hours will resume on January 4, 24th year of the Republic. The receipt and payment of funds by the brokers within the year, starting from December 25, will all use the 29th day bank notes.

Imported Soybean Oil Tax Actually Collected

| Market Price Increased by Sixty to Seventy Cents |

Yesterday, the soybean oil and peanut oil markets surged with rumors that the National Government was requested to reduce or eliminate import taxes on oil from Dong Province. However, this hope was dashed as domestic oil manufacturers and others vigorously opposed the measure. Therefore, the full 30% tariff (30 out of 100) had to be levied. With sources dwindling during this river closure period, market sentiment was unanimously reactive, and the market was filled with tension. As a result, soybean oil increased by fifty to sixty cents, and peanut oil by seventy cents. Peanut oil currently has no base inventory and can only be sold as it arrives. Soybean oil still has some inventory, but the total amount, large and small, is only over ten thousand pieces. Yesterday, statistics showed 700 pieces of peanut oil and 1,000 pieces of soybean oil opened for sale.

Lack of Spot White Tung Oil in Hankou

Over the past half-month, foreign firms in Hankou have been continuously purchasing white tung oil, causing the price to resist falling even during the peak season for new oil. Despite purchases in various producing areas, the supply in Hankou is not very strong, seemingly indicating that supply cannot meet demand. Therefore, spot oil is in great demand. Foreign firms' prices have reached 30 yuan (foreign currency) per dan. If there were a large quantity of spot oil, an additional forty to sixty cents could be added, and some foreign firms are willing to purchase it. Traders quote around 22.5 yuan for oil from Xiangyang and Tongbai, and 25.34 yuan per barrel, including tax. However, only a few hundred dan have arrived. Large shipments are extremely rare because foreign firms are intercepting the oil at the production areas. Consequently, arrivals in Hankou are scarce. There is a relatively large amount of production along the Zhejiang-Jiangxi railway in Jinhua and Lanxi, but the quality is insufficient and can only be used for domestic sales. Foreign firms dislike the insufficient quality, so even with a strong market, their goods are slow to move. Although local firms in this port have managed to purchase some, it is not a large amount. Foreign firms are currently purchasing oil everywhere, so the future market, even if..., is limited.

Noodle Thread: Longkou Noodles Follow Hankou's Price Increase

Recently, in the Longkou noodle thread market, the weather in the production area has become increasingly cold, making it difficult to continue production. Therefore, the market is tightening. According to yesterday's telegrams, the price was initially 28.5 yuan, then 28.7 yuan, and finally rose to 29 yuan, an increase of seventy to eighty cents per package compared to the previous settlement. Consequently, the Shanghai market is following closely. Northern-standard is quoted at 23 yuan, with sales above 22.5 yuan, and Southern-standard also requires more than 21 yuan. Currently, sales are in season, and the future market may tighten further.

Silk and Tea: The First Silk Auction at the San Francisco Exchange

| Spot Goods to be Auctioned Next Year |

As previously reported in this newspaper, Chinese silk can also be delivered and traded alongside raw silk at the San Francisco Exchange's auction. We now have official confirmation that the exchange, which was scheduled to open on the 17th of this month, has commenced operations as scheduled. Forward contracts are being traded first, with spot goods and current month contracts scheduled to begin on January 24th of next year. Shanghai has not yet officially disseminated market prices from the exchange. Today, we obtained a telegram from private sources, which shows the auction prices on the opening day, as follows. Although the prices are outdated, they are worth commemorating. (Price per pound in US dollars)

Opening Price Closing Price

March (Next Year) 1.165 1.1775

July 1.195 1.185

September 1.20 1.19

October 1.20 1.19

December 1.20 1.19

A total of 700 bales were traded that day.

Securities: Both Long and Short Positions Adjusting, Public Bonds Showing Mixed Gains and Losses

Yesterday, at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, this month's futures contracts were nearing their final one or two days. There were still some positions in the market that had not been squared, so position adjustments were particularly active. Retail arbitrage trading also remained very enthusiastic. The trend is temporarily diverging from the environment. Each side is taking its own course based on its own supply and demand dynamics for long and short positions. Therefore, the high price of foreign exchange at four cents is no longer a matter of concern. The Sino-American loan, which is in the works, is not as straightforward as previously reported. It is possibly true that HSBC plans to ship back 20 million taels of silver from Hong Kong. However, whether it will be circulated in the market is still a question. The government is making every effort to maintain silver supply and take into consideration all aspects. In the near future, there will certainly be proper measures to stabilize the market. The public bond market is relatively stable, and the trend is gradually improving. The account balances for this month are only about 30 million, while forward contracts have accumulated to 50 million. Therefore, there should not be much turbulence under the current circumstances. Today is the last day of this month's contracts, and there may still be some infighting. Yesterday, the market opened with a unanimous increase. Bonds No. 16, 20, and 21, etc., were all being bought, and arbitrage trading was also surging. There were few sellers in the market, with increases of about ten to twenty cents to half a yuan. Market prices gradually returned to a moderate state. In the second session, bonds No. 43, 48, and 53, etc., were again being sold, mostly by bulls from last week. Market prices suddenly and uniformly declined, becoming more intense as the day progressed. The 22nd Customs bond fell sharply by eight and a half cents, mostly due to bulls adjusting positions downward. Most of the losses exceeded the gains from the morning session. In the afternoon, the situation stabilized. However, the opening prices listed earlier fell following the morning trend, and bulls again adjusted positions. The settlement for this month suddenly fell by six cents. Since the short-term gold bond, bonds No. 16 and 20 again had short positions being adjusted, and market prices slowly rebounded by three to four cents, gradually narrowing the gap between highs and lows. Closing reports indicated that 20 million taels of silver were being returned to Shanghai. Bond No. 4 was bought, and the settlement rebounded by four and a half cents. The remaining bonds also improved by two to three cents. As a result, market prices varied due to the different decisions made by bulls and bears when adjusting positions, with most gains outweighing losses by about thirty to fifty cents. The total trading volume was about 20 million or more. The resulting gains and losses are listed in the comparative table below (unit: yuan):
